It had been two weeks since Agatha kissed Rio on the balcony and then, for reasons she hadn’t fully justified even to herself, decided not to kiss her again.

 

They hadn’t talked about it. Which, in Agatha’s opinion, was technically different from how things would’ve gone ten years ago. It was just easier to let it exist somewhere else. This was different. It was space. Breathing room. A mutual pause. Acknowledged, if only by the fact that neither of them pretended it hadn’t happened. And that, Agatha told herself, was something. 

 

She’d stayed the night, that first time. On the couch. With Rio. Which wasn’t romantic so much as logistical… and incredibly stupid. They'd both insisted it was fine, and then promptly not slept. At some point, Rio’s arm had ended up across her legs, the blanket twisted halfway off the couch, and Agatha had woken up sore, annoyed, and still not ready to leave.

 

Agatha hung around the next morning. Rio made her coffee, which she begrudgingly admitted was leagues better than the sad, watery excuse her Keurig had been churning out for months. Then Rio made breakfast like it was no big deal -eggs, toast, something green Agatha absolutely refused to identify- and somehow, neither of them commented on the fact that she hadn’t left yet.

 

Agatha didn’t end up leaving until sometime after one. On her way out, she hovered by Rio’s curved bookcase, pretending not to stare at the photo of her, Rio, and Jen in Rio’s old apartment. 

 

Agatha glanced toward the hallway. Rio was still in her room, on the phone with Sage, her voice was muffled.

 

Without thinking, Agatha reached for the frame and slipped it into her bag.

 

It wasn’t a power move. Or petty. She just… wanted it. Like how people steal rocks from beaches or pens from restaurants. Except this one had her face on it, so she figured that made it fair game.

 

Rio came out just as Agatha was sliding the photo into her bag. Agatha looked up and offered her best no, I did not just commit mild sentimental theft smile.

 

If Rio noticed the empty space on the shelf, she didn’t mention it.

 

Rio walked her to her car. And Agatha got in. Drove off. Didn’t look back.

 

The photo stayed tucked in her bag, pressing lightly against her side the whole way home.

 

After that, they kept seeing each other.

 

Not every day. But often enough that it stopped feeling incidental. The thing they’d fallen into didn’t feel like a return to the past- it felt like a negotiation. Like Agatha was learning what it meant to let someone back in without forfeiting ground.

 

She’d been to Rio’s place three times since that morning. Once for dinner. Once while Rio did laundry and Agatha pretended to read. And once for no reason at all- just to be there. That one sat with Agatha the longest.

 

Rio had come over, too. Helped her put together a shelf, though it was less collaborative and more Agatha watching while Rio quietly did all the work. They ate takeout on the floor and put on a movie neither of them cared about. Agatha could barely remember the title. What she remembered was the way their knees stayed pressed together the entire time.

 

They didn’t kiss again.

 

But there were touches that didn’t excuse themselves. Glances that lingered a second too long. A knee brushing hers under a table. Fingers grazing across a countertop. Rio’s palm resting between Agatha’s shoulder blades when she leaned forward to say something in a loud room.

 

They went to game night separately. Sat next to each other anyway. Agatha laughed too hard at something Rio said and had to excuse herself.  She didn’t come back until her face stopped betraying her. She avoided the pointed stares from Jen and Alice for the rest of the night, both of whom looked ready to extract confessions through physical force if necessary.

 

One Sunday, there was a special breakfast with coworkers. Agatha had invited her on the walk to Agatha’s car. It was a passing offer, barely even a sentence but Rio’s face had lit up so entirely unfiltered and stupidly honest. Rio tried to smother it, tried to play it cool, but Agatha had already seen it. 

 

Agatha had to look away. Her chest was too full. Rio’s face alone had nearly taken her out.

 

Rio ended up across from her at the table, then next to her when someone else wanted the seat so they could talk to Jen. Their knees touched under the table. Neither of them moved.

 

And still, they hadn’t kissed again.

 

It would’ve been easy. That was the thing. It would’ve been so goddamn easy to lean in. To let it happen again, under the right conditions, with the right excuse.

 

But Agatha didn’t.

 

And this wasn’t because she was spiraling. This wasn’t slipping back into a version of them that had already failed once. She’d kissed Rio three times- once would’ve been forgivable, twice unfortunate, but three? That was a pattern. That was admitting she wanted more. So she didn’t do it again. She didn’t ask. Didn’t lean in. She told herself she was being careful. Smart.

 

But some days, the panic still curled around her spine- hot, insistant, hard to ignore. Not about the past but about what this might be turning into. About the terrifying possibility that they were actually doing something right this time.

 

So she kept space in her life on purpose. Made time for herself. Said yes to drinks with Jen. Spent her evenings at the gym, earbuds in, volume high. She didn’t cut herself off from Rio, but she didn’t disappear into it either.

 

Agatha needed to believe she had kept something of herself untouched. Just so there’d be something left of her to walk away with incase this ended. 

 

Then maybe Agatha could say it hadn’t meant everything. 

 

Even if it had.

 

But deep down, beneath every lie Agatha could almost believe, something quieter lived: the certainty that what was untouched had already been seen. And worse- welcomed.

 

-

 

Agatha sat cross legged on the bed, the bottle of black nail polish uncapped on a towel between them. She had just started painting Rio’s left hand, holding it gently as she dragged the brush across each nail. The other hand, already finished, rested on her knee. It had been there for a while. Neither of them mentioned it.

 

Rio was still, suspiciously still, as she painted. 

 

Agatha said nothing. She kept her eyes down, painting each nail with careful, practiced strokes.

 

Rio, of course, couldn’t let that last.

 

“Let’s play twenty questions,” Rio said, casually. 

 

“No,” Agatha said without looking up.

 

 “Cool. I’ll go first.”

 

Agatha exhaled through her nose. “That’s not-”

 

“Am I bad kisser?”

 

The brush paused, mid air. Agatha blinked once, then looked up, “Why?”



Rio shrugged, eyes sliding to the side.  “Oh, well. You know. Someone asked, and I thought- hm. Why don’t I ask Ag-”

 

“Who the fuck is wondering about your kissing skills?”

 

Rio blinked, caught off guard. “What? No- no one important. And that wasn’t the question.”

 

Agatha’s jaw locked. Her vision whitened at the edges. She wasn’t jealous. That would have required giving a fuck. It was just ridiculous. Who asked something like that? Who thought they could?

 

“You don’t get to skip mine,” Agatha said flatly.

 

“I asked first! It’s a yes or no question. So… yes or no. Am I a good kisser?”

 

“I just don’t get why someone needs to know. Like is there a follow up planned? Are they trying to kiss y-”

 

Agatha caught the end of the question as it twisted out of her mouth. She didn’t stop because she lost her nerve. She stopped because she finally heard how she had sounded. The edge in her voice wasn’t neutral. It was personal, and it was obvious. Her own question wasn’t about the game anymore.

 

Rio said nothing. Only looked at Agatha, shoulders loose, lips pressed together like she might smile, like she might say more if Agatha gave her an inch.

 

Agatha turned back to the bottle. Tapped the brush once against the rim.

 

“I didn’t know it was up for peer review,” she muttered, and moved on to Rio’s middle finger. 

 

“No one’s asked,” Rio admitted quietly. 

 

Agatha felt something in her shoulders let go. She pressed her bottom lip between her teeth, held it there, and didn’t say anything. It was a stupid thing to feel relieved about. She felt it anyway.

 

Rio shifted. and Agatha could feel her staring.

 

“I just… think maybe you aren’t answering because… I don’t know.”

 

Agatha exhaled through her nose and kept her gaze locked on Rio’s hand.

 

“We haven’t, you know. Since-”

 

Agatha didn’t take the bait. Just moved on to the next finger. Perfect strokes. Steady hand. Her face, however, was getting warm.

 

Rio cleared her throat. “It’s fine if you don’t want to. I just… figured if it was because I sucked, I’d rather know.”

 

Agatha squeezed Rio’s hand with more pressure than necessary. It wasn’t a mistake. It was a warning. 

 

“Ow,” Rio said lightly, trying to make a joke of it. “Cool. Torture me in silence.”

 

“You’re the one who brought it up,” Agatha muttered. 

 

“Because we kissed.”

 

Agatha finally looked up, brows raised. “And now you want me to give you a grade on it?” 

 

Rio flushed and looked away. “Forget it.”

 

Agatha went back to painting, jaw tight. The next nail came out smudged. She wiped it clean and started again.

 

Fuck, she was annoyed. Annoyed that for one stupid second, she thought someone else had wanted to kiss Rio. Annoyed that it got to her. Annoyed at the way Rio’s big, miserable brown eyes burning a hole straight through her forehead. And most of all, she was annoyed because the hand resting on her knee had gone slack -like Rio had pulled away, or was about to- and that ache in her chest wasn’t subtle anymore.

 

Agatha hated the whole thing. The look. The silence. The part of her that cared. She knew she was being unfair. 

 

“Just so you know,” Agatha said flatly, not looking up, “you’re not bad at it.”

 

“Oh,” Rio said, trying and failing not to sound too pleased. “Okay.”

 

Two seconds of silence.

 

“Are we gonna kiss again?”

 

Agatha looked at her then.

 

Of course she wanted to kiss Rio again. She always had. That had been the problem from the very start. It wasn’t just once, or twice, or the last time. It was every version of her. Every glance across a room. Every time they got too close to saying something they shouldn’t. Every silence that squeezed tight like a hand around a throat.

 

There had never been a version of Rio Agatha didn’t want.

 

That was the part Agatha could never quite make peace with. It never dulled, never gave her room to outgrow.  And somehow, it still caught her off guard. Every single time.

 

She looked down at the last nail and corrected a smudge that wasn’t there. It gave her something to do. Something to control.

 

“If I say yes, will you stop talking?”

 

“Yes.”

 

Agatha narrowed her eyes. “Fine. Then yes.”

 

Rio smiled. “That a real yes?”

 

Agatha stood. “It’s a shut up before I change my mind yes.”

 

“Still counts.”

 

Agatha didn’t look back. But her ears were warm. And she absolutely knew it still counted.

 

She took the bottle of black polish and walked into the bathroom.

 

The drawer was already open. Everything inside was lined up- nail files, cotton pads, cuticle oil, everything in its place. The polish had a designated spot.

 

Agatha stared at it for a second too long, then set the bottle down and closed the drawer quietly.

 

When she came back, Rio was leaned back against the headboard, legs stretched out, watching some documentary about the ocean.

 

Agatha sat beside her. Not too close. Not far either. She tried to focus on the screen.

 

A narrator droned on about migration patterns and instinct. Something about the way certain fish followed the same path every year, even when they didn’t know why.

 

Agatha crossed her arms.

 

“You know,” Rio said, eyes not leaving the screen. 

 

Agatha kept her gaze forward, but every part of her had turned toward the sound of Rio’s voice. It always did. 

 

“I quite like kissing you.”

 

And Agatha hated how her pulse reacted.

 

For years, everything between them had existed in what they didn’t say. That was how they survived it- through silence, through the comfort of what never had to be spoken. That was the one thing Rio had always understood. She used to live inside it with Agatha, as if the quiet was sacred.

 

But lately, Rio had started breaking the rules. She had started letting the quiet fill up with real words. Saying things out loud that were never supposed to be spoken. Things they used to leave alone.

 

Agatha hadn’t figured out how to stay intact when that happened. She could manage silence. She was built for it. But this left her exposed in ways she didn’t know how to cover.

 

Though Rio had figured it out, hadn’t she? That if she talked enough, Agatha wouldn’t have anywhere left to hide.

 

And if there was nowhere left to hide, it got harder to move anywhere that wasn’t toward Rio. 

 

Agatha thought about answering. She thought about denying it or joking or acting like she hadn’t heard. But none of those options felt available anymore. Not when Rio said things like that without fear.

 

So Agatha stayed where she was, her posture careful, her jaw set.

 

“Okay,” Agatha said, as evenly as she could manage.

 

A moment passed. Rio reached over and rested her hand on Agatha’s thigh, fingers splayed gentle and careful, mindful not to smear the half dry polish on her nails. Her thumb pressed into Agatha’s thigh. 

 

Agatha didn’t move. She didn’t breathe too hard. She told herself not to react.

 

Then Rio spoke again.

 

“Do you want me to keep talking?” she asked, softly.

 

Agatha let her gaze drop to Rio’s hand resting on her thigh. She followed the shape of it- the curve of Rio’s knuckles, the pale blue veins running up her wrist, the black polish Agatha had painted there. It was perfect. Hers.

 

She shouldn’t have cared about that detail. But she did.

 

It was proof of something. Another mark that was Agatha’s. Another small thing added to a life that hadn’t felt like hers in a long time. Not when she was married. Not when she was making decisions that belonged to other people. But this- this was different. Agatha had put that color there. Her hands had made it so.

 

Agatha swallowed hard and looked back at the screen. She forced herself to breathe evenly. 

 

Agatha nodded once.

 

Because yes. She wanted Rio to keep talking. She wanted to hear every word she’d missed, every thought Rio hadn’t said until now. She wanted it so badly it made her ache. But the only thing she could give her was that single, careful nod.

 

Rio didn’t look at her, kept her eyes fixed on the screen. Her thumb stayed still, pressing into Agatha’s skin. “I want to kiss you again,” Rio said softly. “I think about it all the time. More than I probably should.” 

 

Agatha inhaled, eyes fluttering shut.

 

Rio was a siren, and Agatha would follow her straight into the ocean if it meant that voice was the last thing she ever heard.

Agatha’s eyes didn’t move from the board. She could feel the heat in her neck immediately, the pressure building behind her eyes and in the tight corners of her jaw. She didn’t want to respond. She wanted to keep pretending she had the upper hand, that she was the one who had walked away unaffected, that she hadn’t been mentally screaming since the moment Rio stopped paying attention to her.

 

“I’m not mad,” Agatha muttered, voice stiff and entirely unconvincing.

 

“Sure,” Rio said simply.

 

“I’m not,” Agatha repeated, now fully aware of how juvenile she sounded but too deep in it to stop.

 

“Okay.”

 

That was it. That was all she got. 

 

Agatha half turned her body, whipped her head around, and stared at Rio fucking stunned.

 

Rio was just standing there. Relaxed. Polite.

 

Agatha turned back slowly, jaw clenched, pulse thrumming in her throat. She wanted to scream.

 

“You’re pissing me off,” Agatha snapped.

 

“I’m doing what you wanted,” Rio replied, calm as anything.

 

“Well, it’s pissing me off.”

 

Rio hummed, like that amused her. “Come smoke with me.”

 

“No.” She folded her arms tighter. “I don’t think I will.”

 

“Agatha.”

 

And just like that, Agatha’s body betrayed her. Her shoulders eased, barely, as though they’d been waiting for permission. That tone. That inflection. No one else ever said her name like that. She didn’t answer. She let her eyes close, slow and controlled, maybe if she moved carefully enough she wouldn’t have to acknowledge what it did to her.

 

Rio stepped in, too close now, her breath warm at the shell of Agatha’s ear. Not touching, but close enough to feel it.

 

“I miss you,” Rio whispered.

 

Agatha’s lip curled. That was better.

 

“I know.”

 

Rio hadn’t moved. Was still standing there, probably poking her tongue against the inside of her cheek the way she always did when she didn’t know if she was losing or winning.

 

Good. Let her wonder.

 

Agatha didn’t say anything else right away. She let the silence stretch, let the tension settle again. She liked the way Rio was holding still, like any sudden movement might ruin it.

 

“You gonna say something else that’ll make me feel better, or just stand there breathing on me?”

 

“You want me to beg?” Rio said, voice infuriatingly steady.

 

“I don’t care what you do,” Agatha shot back, adding a shrug for effect. Unbothered. Not insanely aware of how turned on she was. Not at all.

 

There was a pause. Then Rio leaned in, closer than she had all night, her body leaning in just enough to press up against Agatha’s back. Not hands. Not hips. Just the faint pressure of crossed arms brushing against the middle of Agatha’s back- light, contained, like she was trying not to touch her at all and failing on purpose.  

 

“Stay at my place tonight,” Rio said, soft. 

 

Agatha smirked.  She could feel Rio straining under all that self control, her body betraying her in the smallest, most satisfying ways. And fuck, it felt like winning.

 

“Oh, I don’t know,” Agatha said lightly, loading it with just enough condescension to make herself feel powerful. “We have work tomorrow.”

 

And she expected that to be the end of it. Expected Rio to back off. To take the hit and behave, like she’d been doing all night. Good girl. Gold star.

 

But then- 

 

“Please.”

 

It wasn’t even a word. Not really. Just breath, hot against her ear, low and dangerous and too fucking soft.

 

“Please, baby. I’ll do anything.”

 

Agatha made a sound. It wasn’t intentional. Wasn’t dignified. It punched out of her in a pathetic little gasp- high in her throat, half a whimper, half a groan, fully, irreparably fucking humiliating.

 

She went still.

 

Fully frozen. Eyes wide, chest locked, brain freshly wiped by the horny wrath of god.

 

Alright. Wrap it up. Wrap it the fuck up, Agatha. 

 

“Fine,” she snapped, too loud and too fast, already turning away like the sound hadn’t come from her at all. Because if she didn’t walk off right then -immediately, with purpose- she was going to do something catastrophic. Something irreversible. Something she would absolutely not be able to explain to security.

 

She stormed back toward their group with her jaw tight and her hands clenched into fists at her sides, walking like she hadn’t just nearly collapsed because a woman said please.

 

It was fine.

 

She was fine.

 

Totally calm. Totally in control. Definitely not seconds away from hauling Rio into the nearest disgusting bowling alley bathroom and dropping to her knees. 

 

Jesus Christ.

 

Agatha needed a Diet Coke and a fucking lobotomy.

 

-

 

Agatha was standing, grabbing the last of her shit, counting down the seconds until she could get out of this godforsaken neon lit purgatory with Rio.

 

Rio was on the far side of their section, leaned up against the plastic high top counter. It was one of those built in setups, too high to sit at comfortably, with stools and the open racks underneath for bowling balls, like some bastardization of a bar and a storage unit. She had her arms crossed loosely, talking to Sage and Alice like nothing was out of place. Like she hadn’t whispered ‘ please, baby. I’ll do anything.’ against Agatha’s ear earlier and then gone right back to looking like a smug, patient son of a bitch.

 

Agatha had tried - tried - desperately not to notice her. Not to track every change in posture, every glance, every small movement that reminded her exactly how far she was from losing control in public. It hadn’t worked. Of course it hadn’t. Rio was right there, in the same goddamn bowling alley, being hot and polite and pretending like she didn’t know Agatha was one more breath away from losing her shit.

 

Teen was on the couch beside her, talking at length about… Agatha doesn’t fucking know. But she was nodding along like she could hear it. She couldn't. She was too busy focusing on the clock, on her breath, on the promise of being done with this place and in Rio’s car. The night was almost over. She was almost free.

 

And then- 

 

“Agatha?”

 

She felt her stomach drop so violently she was sure she had just shit it out of her own asshole. 

 

It came from the wrong direction. It came from a voice that should not, under any circumstances, have been here.

 

Agatha turned slowly, already knowing what she would see and still unprepared for it.

 

Wanda.

 

Not in Chicago.

 

Here.

 

In the middle of a bowling alley in fucking Westview, New Jersey.

 

Agatha stared at her ex-wife, eyes locked and expression neutral, even as her brain started screaming: No, I want more time!

 

It was grief, like something sacred being ripped out by its roots. A primal, internal protest against the inevitability that nothing Wanda touched ever survived. Even permanence learned to wilt beneath it. 

 

“Can we talk?” Wanda asked, soft.

 

Agatha stared at her, mouth dry, heart shredding through her chest. She didn’t have an answer.

 

Still, her fingers twitched -just barely, just once- in the direction of Rio Vidal, who was not looking at her. Of course. Classic. Same reach as before. Still pathetic. Still unanswered. And yet, apparently, her body hadn’t gotten the memo, because here it was again. Subtle. Stupid. Waiting around like a little idiot, just in case Rio fucking Vidal wanted to notice this time.

 

This was what it looked like when the universe put a hand between her shoulder blades and whispered, ‘You don’t get to have that.’

 

But Agatha saw it in her periphery- a blur of motion veering straight toward her ex-wife. She didn’t bother looking. Just let her eyes fall shut and waited.

 

A shout followed. Wanda’s voice, loud with disbelief. 

 

When Agatha opened her eyes, Rio was standing in front of her. A little out of breath from crossing the room. Or maybe from thirteen years of trying to get here in time.

 

“Hey,” Rio said, still a little winded. “Sorry I’m late.”

 

Rio turned to look behind her. Agatha followed her gaze- Wanda, soaked. Sage crouched beside the fallen pitcher, scrambling, mouthing a series of apologies that couldn’t have sounded less genuine. Beer everywhere.

 

Rio looked back at Agatha, a small smile pulling at her mouth like she didn’t regret a single second of it.

 

“Had to improvise.” Rio said, with a shrug that felt too easy to be innocent. She reached out slightly, a fingertip grazing the back of Agatha’s hand. “Let’s go back to mine, yeah?”

 

 

Chapter End Notes

the way i wanted to end this chapter at 'you don't get to have that' but literally could not stomach the idea of even teasing that Rio wasn't paying attention... literally made me sick.

anyway, writing this chapter fucking sucked and i feel a bit meh about it. this entire story was supposed to be far angstier than it is but every time i sit down to write, my gf is whispering into my ear: 'you will not hurt them' (threat)

i love you, i'm sorry

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

“Rio?” Agatha whispered.

 

None of it felt real. The sounds, the lights, the clatter of pins- it all fell away. All she could feel was the flood in her chest, unasked for but absolute, at the sight of her. That dumb, beautiful face Agatha had been pretending to outrun, while tracing its outline in every life that never felt like hers.

 

“Yeah,” Rio breathed. “I’m sorry it took me so long.” She said it again, quieter this time, as her pointer finger reached out and curled around Agatha’s.

 

“I-“ Agatha started, but stopped. She swallowed, glancing over Rio’s shoulder. Sage was making an absolute scene, and somehow, Wanda looked genuinely rattled by it.

 

Good. 

 

She looked back. Rio hadn’t looked away.

 

“Get me the fuck out of here.”

 

“My fucking pleasure,” Rio said, a breath of relief slipping through her grin as she grabbed Agatha’s hand fully. 

 

Rio’s hand tightened around her own, her thumb brushed across her knuckles, and tugged gently, coaxing Agatha to follow.

 

They wove through the mess of rental shoes and drunk adults. Rio didn’t stop. Not even when someone shouted “Hey! Private party!” 

 

They’d just made it to the carpet when Agatha heard it. It came from behind them, cutting through the noise with an ease that made Agatha’s stomach turn.

 

“Didn’t think you had it in you, Vidal! Honestly, I’m impressed. After our last conversation, when you slunked off with your tail tucked, I figured you’d have the sense to stay gone.”

 

Rio stopped cold.

 

Agatha walked directly into her back and startled at the contact, but Rio didn’t budge. For a second, she thought she had misheard.

 

Last conversation.

 

The word landed like a misstep on a staircase- ordinary until it wasn’t, until her stomach dropped and nothing made sense.

 

What the fuck was Wanda talking about?

 

Agatha blinked, trying to make sense of it. Wanda’s words didn’t fit anywhere. They bounced and bumped against her skull like that old 3D Space Cadet pinball game she used to play on her mother’s computer. Flashing lights and endless dings, where once the ball started moving, you just sat there and watched it spiral out of control.

 

Agatha’s chest tightened. Her skin went cold.

 

And then Rio’s hand was no longer in hers.

 

Agatha turned because she always did. Because she had learned to chase the silence without ever meaning to. A reflex. Her heart, stupid and unrelenting, lurched after Rio like it always did- clawing, screaming, desperate to be held by the only hands it had ever called home.

 

She looked, just in time to see Rio moving straight toward Wanda. Her jaw was locked. Her fists were curled. Her shoulders were squared in a way Agatha had never seen before.

 

That was the part that rattled Agatha most.

 

She had spent years trying to get a rise out of Rio for fun. She had pushed her, cornered her, just trying to get her to react. To snap. To yell. Anything. But Rio had always been infuriatingly calm. Even in their worst moments, she never looked like this.

 

There was no mask left. Just a fury so sharp it looked like it didn’t belong to her.

 

Agatha stood frozen, caught in utter disbelief. 

 

Wanda’s shirt was soaked through, clinging to her chest. She looked wrecked and triumphant, like someone who had nothing left to lose and had decided to aim carefully.

 

“Rio!”

 

Agatha saw Sage scramble upright, already moving before Rio could take another step.

 

“Don’t!” Sage shouted, and then she crashed into Rio with her full weight, arms hooking around her shoulders, with a force that made Agatha flinch.

 

A thud, a breath knocked loose, the squeak of shoes. They staggered back, off balance for a second, but didn’t fall.

 

“You stupid, miserable fucking cunt!” Rio yelled over Sage’s shoulder, her voice loud enough to draw attention.

 

Pins clattered somewhere in the distance. A child near the snack counter started crying. Music still played overhead, far too cheerful for what had just been said.

 

It was the first time Agatha had ever heard Rio raise her voice like that.

 

Sage shoved Rio. Hard. “Hey- get a grip,” she snapped.

 

“Rio!” Agatha shouted.

 

That single word pulled Rio’s gaze immediately. She looked at Agatha, breathing hard. Still furious. Still shaking.

 

Her eyes were wild- glassy, burning, like she was barely holding herself together. And for a heartbeat, Agatha didn’t recognize her.

 

Not this version.

 

This was not the person who used to tuck every feeling away behind a mask, who could disarm with a glance and disappear behind silence before anyone got too close.

 

That Rio was gone. Burned through, actually.

 

Who stood in front of Agatha now was raw and exposed, rage crackling beneath her skin and carved into the lock of her jaw.

 

Agatha held her gaze.

 

“You’re done,” Agatha said softly. “Come with me.”

 

For a breath, nothing.

 

And then Rio exhaled and gave a single nod.

 

Agatha lifted her arm and signaled Rio forward.

 

Rio moved.

 

They walked together, shoulder to shoulder, past stunned faces and spilled beer, past the blur of noise behind them. Agatha heard Wanda call her name. She didn’t turn around. She kept her eyes ahead, her pace steady.

 

Two security guards brushed past them, heading toward the noise. Somewhere behind, Jen’s voice rang out, sharp and clear. Then Alice, angrier, more direct. Agatha didn’t look back. Her friends had it handled.

 

“Agatha!” Wanda again, louder now. “Don’t you dare leave with her!”

 

Rio was at her side, then slightly ahead of her. She was breathing hard.

 

“I’m your wife!”

 

Rio’s stride lengthened. Her jaw was still tight. Agatha didn’t need to see her face to know what that voice was doing to her. She could feel it. Every part of Rio’s body was tense, she was holding herself in check, every step a decision not to turn around and make it worse.

 

They rounded the corner.

 

The sounds behind them dulled. The light changed. The entrance’s atrium was quieter, colder. Rio kept moving. She was several steps ahead now, walking fast, like her body was trying to outrun her mind.

 

Whatever Wanda had meant by ‘ last conversation’, Agatha had no idea. It didn’t make sense. Rio and Wanda had barely ever spoke. That much Agatha knew. If anything ever happened between them, it happened when Agatha wasn’t looking because she hadn’t thought she needed to look.

 

Agatha didn’t know what was true. She didn’t know what Rio had kept from her.

 

And now wasn’t the time to find out.

 

Priorities , Agatha reminded herself. First: out. Then: Rio.

 

Because right now, Rio was still walking ahead of her because she needed to be somewhere else before she could breathe properly.  She needed distance. From the building. From the shouting. From whatever scar had torn open inside her and started to bleed.

 

Agatha would wait. She would walk behind her, through this ugly stretch of silence, until the shaking in Rio’s hands stopped.

 

Rio barreled through the double doors, her stride relentless, but even then, she paused just long enough to hold the door open for Agatha. A gentleman, to the last. Not that Rio waited for thanks. The moment Agatha stepped through, Rio turned away and cut across the parking lot with purposeful steps that didn’t once falter or look back. 

 

They reached the car. Agatha slowed, arms folding loosely over her chest as she watched Rio. 

 

Rio flung the driver’s side door open and ducked inside.  Her hand reappeared with a battered pack of cigarettes, one of which she shoved between her teeth before slamming the door shut behind her. She leaned back against the car like it was the only thing keeping her upright and brought the purple zippo to her mouth, fingers trembling so violently the flame refused to catch. Once. Twice. Three times. Still nothing.

 

“Fuck,” Rio snapped. Her voice had gone hoarse somewhere in all of this.

 

Agatha approached slowly. She set her purse beside Rio’s feet and moved in front of her. The streetlight caught the edges of Rio’s face, but she  refused to look at Agatha. She kept trying to light the cigarette with growing frustration, her jaw tight, her focus narrowed to the task.

 

“Rio,” Agatha said quietly.

 

No response. Just the click of metal and a flicker that never turned into flame.

 

She reached out and gently took the lighter from Rio’s hand, expecting a protest, a scoff, a flinch- anything. But Rio let her. Her fingers uncurled so easily it made Agatha ache. She flicked the lighter once. The flame caught instantly. Rio leaned forward, inhaled, and let the smoke fill her lungs. Again. And again. She pulled the cigarette away, dropped her head back against the car, and exhaled into the sky with her neck exposed and her jaw clenched.

 

The skin of Rio’s neck caught the light- some of the concealer Agatha had aggressively applied earlier had worn thin. Not all of it, but just enough for Agatha to see what was underneath.

 

And oh, how Agatha wanted to reach out and wipe the rest away. Strip it down to truth. To Rio’s truth. To hers. And God, part of Agatha wanted to rewind time to this morning. To yesterday. To every moment before their bubble popped. But it wouldn’t help. Wanting never did.

 

So, Agatha did the next best thing and stepped forward until their bodies touched. Until she could feel Rio flinch in surprise. Her head snapped down and suddenly brown eyes locked onto Agatha’s- endless, pleading without asking for anything.

 

Agatha let her own body soften, tension draining from her frame because, somehow, Rio’s pain had always made more sense than her own. 

 

She reached up and took the baseball cap off Rio’s head, let it fall with the lighter on top of her purse. Then both hands lifted to cup Rio’s face. Softly. Carefully. Tender in a way that made herself want to cry. 

 

Rio’s free hand flew up to clutch Agatha’s wrist, as if she were afraid this was a dream she’d wake from too soon.

 

Agatha tucked strands of Rio’s hair behind her ears. Her fingers found their way into the roots, lifting to the back of her head, guiding her in. She pulled Rio into a hug. One arm curled around her shoulders, the other cradling the back of her head. 

 

Rio didn’t fight it. She gave in completely- slackening against Agatha’s chest and letting her breath shudder out against her skin.

 

Agatha felt the press of Rio’s mouth against her shoulder first- soft, seeking, not quite steady. One arm wrapped firmly around Agatha’s waist while the other remained limp at her side. 

 

Then came the faint sound of a dull hiss of ember meeting pavement. The cigarette. Rio let it go. 

 

A moment later, both arms were circled around Agatha’s back, drawing her closer with desperation.

 

Agatha melted into Rio. Pressed every part of herself forward until there was no space left between them. Her face leaned into the side of Rio’s head, and for a moment they stood like that, almost swaying.

 

Eventually, Agatha finally pulled back, it wasn’t much, barely an inch, just enough to see Rio’s mouth, her eyelashes, the tiny tremble in her lip. Her hand found the side of Rio’s face, her thumb grazing her cheek. Agatha dipped her head, slow and cautious, letting the tip of her nose brush against Rio’s.

 

Rio nodded. Fast. Breath catching in her throat like it hurt.

 

Agatha kissed her.

 

She pressed her mouth into Rio’s with no force, no urgency. It didn’t come with heat or hunger, only stillness. 

 

Agatha didn’t want anything from her. She didn’t need anything. She only wanted to erase whatever her ex-wife had ripped open and remind Rio, gently, that Agatha was here.  

 

She pulled back slightly, just enough to breathe, and then kissed Rio again- softer this time. Then her mouth found the corner of Rio’s lips. Then her cheek. Then the place just beneath her ear, where her jawline gave way to her throat. Each kiss pressed with a purpose.

 

When Agatha’s lips found Rio’s again, she stayed for a moment. Then pulled back just far enough to whisper, “I’m sorry.”

 

Another kiss.

 

“I’m so sorry.”

 

Another.

 

Each apology landed between them as if Agatha’s mouth knew how to beg better than her voice ever could.

 

Rio didn’t speak. She leaned in every time, chasing Agatha, her hands clenched behind Agatha’s back, holding tight, nodding faintly between kisses. Her breath hitched every time Agatha pulled away. Her grip never loosened.

 

And Agatha kept going. She only wanted Rio to stay here- to let go, even if only for a moment. 

 

To let herself be cared for. 

 

And Agatha would stay. As long as it took. As long as Rio needed. 

 

Agatha would stay. 

 

-

 

The drive back to Rio’s apartment was quiet, but not awkward. Rio drove one hand on the wheel, her other hand curled around Agatha’s in her lap, thumb brushing the inside of her palm now and then, like she needed to make sure she was still there. 

 

Agatha had offered to drive but Rio gave her a look so wild and immediate that it bordered on offended. A silent absolutely not paired with an unspoken I’m not letting you kill us before we get home . 

 

Which, fair. Agatha wasn’t exactly known for her driving. It was probably their second longest running joke, right after whatever punchline they’d always been.

 

By the time they got inside, neither of them had said much beyond the necessary. Rio showered first. Agatha followed after, rinsing off everything except the weight that had settled across her chest the second she saw Rio’s body still in that god forsaken bowling alley. 

 

Rio had on a t-shirt, underwear, and socks. Always with the socks. She’d been weird about that for as long as Agatha had known her. Something about not being able to stand the feel of crumbs or dirt on her feet, the horror of some invisible particle touching skin. If she was home, she’d change into a clean pair right before getting into bed, even if the ones she had on were practically new. It wasn’t optional. She never slept without them. Agatha never understood it. Still didn’t. But she’d watched it for so many years, the ritual stopped needing a reason. It was just Rio.

 

Agatha chose to wear one of Rio’s sweatshirts- oversized, soft, lived in, absolutely would be coming home with her- and nothing else but underwear.

 

When Agatha wandered out into the living room, Rio was already sunk into the couch, phone to her ear, murmuring some half distracted responses. “Mm. Uh-uh.” Her eyes flicked up, and without missing a beat, she reached out an arm toward Agatha like she was just getting home- expected, familiar, wanted. Not even a question.

 

Agatha huffed a breath through her nose and moved toward her without a second of hesitation. She sank into the space Rio had made, leaned into the warmth waiting there. 

 

Rio, still on the phone, murmured a quick, “Love you, Petal. Thanks again,” before hanging up and tossing the phone onto the coffee table like it had never existed.

 

She didn’t say it was Sage. Didn’t have to. Agatha already knew.

 

Rio curled into her, one arm slung across Agatha’s stomach, remote in hand, flipping through channels. Agatha mumbled something half hearted about Housewives , and Rio, without protest, put it on.

 

They got maybe fifteen minutes into the episode before Agatha started chewing at her thumbnail. 

 

Not subtle. Not pretty. It was a nervous habit she never quite managed to break. Her eyes stayed on the screen, but her mind had already left the room.

 

Agatha didn’t want to ask. That was the truth of it. She didn’t want to know what Wanda had said to Rio. Not because she was afraid of the answer, but because she already had too many. Too many versions of their story, too many angles on the same wound. The past didn’t need clarifying- it had been clear enough when it hurt. She didn’t want the knife turned again under the excuse of context.

 

Surprisingly, Agatha was good at holding her tongue. Especially about things that mattered. Especially when silence kept her from doing damage. 

 

When it came to pain, Agatha tended to be precise. Efficient. Her cruelty was rarely accidental. She knew exactly how to find the soft spot and press- except with Rio. That was the one place she never quite managed to fully weaponize. And somehow, Wanda had pulled it off in a single conversation. A few words. A single glance. Whatever prior conversation she had referred to, it landed.

 

Agatha felt the question rising again. It had been sitting at the base of her throat since the parking lot. Waiting for any moment to sneak out. But she didn’t give it the room. She swallowed it back down. She didn’t want to drag it between them. Not now.

 

She didn’t want to drag Wanda into this room. Not into Rio’s apartment, not onto this couch, not into the strange, careful space the two of them had managed to build without even directly saying they were trying.

 

It wasn’t until she felt Rio’s fingers gently wrap around her wrist that Agatha had realized she was still biting her nail. Rio gently guided her hand down and didn’t let go. Just held it, thumb tracing over the back of Agatha’s fingers.

 

Then, without even looking away from the TV, she lifted Agatha’s hand and kissed it. Soft. Barely there. Like breathing.

 

And that was it.

 

Agatha’s chest eased without her permission. Her jaw unclenched. Her shoulders finally dropped. It didn’t fix anything, didn’t undo the knot in her stomach, but it quieted her mind. 

 

She let Rio keep holding her hand. Let herself settle. Let the question drift back down to where it came from.

 

It could wait.

 

This couldn’t.

 

-

 

“What if we called out of work this weekend,” Rio murmured. Her cheek was mashed flat against Agatha’s shoulder, as she traced lazy shapes into the back of Agatha's hand.

 

“You don’t call out.” Agatha said, while her other hand moved automatically, smoothing down Rio’s back, fingertips tracing the hem of her t-shirt, eyes fixed on the TV.

 

“I could,” Rio said, slower now. “For a good enough reason.”

 

Agatha let out a small, skeptical laugh. “That so?”

 

Rio didn’t laugh with her. She just nodded into her neck. “Yeah. I don’t know. I thought maybe we could get out of town for a bit… just us.”

 

At first, Agatha hadn’t been sure Rio was serious, but there was something careful in the way Rio said it, like she didn’t want to ask for too much. And that, more than anything, made Agatha answer.

 

“What did you have in mind?”

 

“Swartswood Lake.”

 

Agatha breathed out slowly through her nose. 

 

That made sense. Remote. Quiet. Not too far, but far enough. It wasn’t about the lake. Or the weekend. Or the idea of calling out of work. It was about space. Distance. A place Wanda wouldn’t be. A place where Rio could breathe without checking over her shoulder, and where Agatha wouldn’t have to pretend she was unaffected.

 

“Swartswood,” Agatha repeated.

 

“Never mind,” Rio mumbled. “Dumb idea.” She pressed in closer, burying her face into Agatha’s shoulder like she wanted to disappear there, to make a home out of her and stay hidden.

 

“I didn’t say that,” Agatha replied softly. She slid her hand under the hem of Rio’s shirt, her fingers skimming warm skin before her nails lightly dragged downward.

 

“Oh.” The breath left Rio in a soft puff, barely audible, but Agatha felt it against her collarbone.

 

Genuinely, Agatha didn’t mind the idea. A getaway. Just them. Somewhere far enough that the world couldn’t follow. Somewhere Wanda wouldn’t show up. No group hangouts. No coworkers. No expectations.

 

It sounded... simple. And simplicity had started to feel like luxury.

 

But it also felt like a threat to everything Agatha had so carefully built. Time alone meant space to speak. And space invited honesty. It dismantled excuses. She knew how it would go: long silences, then the questions- first quiet, then louder. And beneath it all, the risk that one of them might actually answer honestly.

 

“I’m not participating in any outdoor activities,” Agatha said finally, voice dry. “No fishing. No glizzy roasting. If you even think about handing me a metal skewer and tell me it builds character, I’ll drown myself in the lake.”

 

Rio’s laugh was sudden, surprised- beautiful. Agatha startled slightly at the sound, bit her lip to kill the smile that tried to follow.

 

“I wouldn’t dream of it,” Rio said, her voice already softer from laughing.

 

“I don’t do tents or any other camping bullshit,” Agatha added flatly, her fingers dragging a little rougher at the base of Rio’s spine as penance for even putting the image in her head.

 

“No tents,” Rio promised. Agatha could hear the grin in her voice. “There’s a lakehouse. Sybil’s place. She bought it a few years ago, rents it out sometimes. It’s beautiful. On the lake. You’d like it.”

 

Sybil.

 

Lilia’s younger sister. Agatha remembered her vividly- silver hair down to her waist, always barefoot, always rich, with no discernible source of income. Looked like she wandered out of a 1970s music video.

 

She was hot. Undeniably so. And Agatha, being twenty-four and chronically annoying, may have announced that within five minutes of meeting her.

 

Rio had lost her mind. Not in any useful, productive way- just sulking and theatrics. Spent the entire weekend accusing Agatha of betrayal and dramatically refusing to pass her things. At one point she even called her a homewrecker, which didn’t even make sense.

Closer to the shoreline, black willow branches leaned low over the bank, their leaves whispering against the surface. A single sycamore stood to the right of the dock, its pale bark flaking in broad patches, casting shifting light through its canopy.

It was beautiful.

Not in a charming, good sport way. She played to win, played to ruin people a little. Rio used to call it fun until Agatha started running the table and pretending it wasn’t personal. It always was. That was the point.

 

They used to play at shitty dive bars, mostly back in Westview, mostly after too many drinks. The tables were always uneven. The cues were warped. Someone would put on bad music and sing along. Rio would flirt with strangers and pretend not to watch Agatha play. Agatha would pretend not to notice any of it. They were best friends. It was fine.

 

Pool had helped. It gave her something to focus on. Something to control. Angles, geometry, force- it was reliable in a way people weren’t. If she played hard enough, she didn’t have to think about the way Rio would hover just behind her during a shot, close enough to breathe on her neck. Or how she'd laugh every time Agatha called a ball and made an entirely different one, then claimed it counted anyway.

 

It had been easier back then. Not simple. Never that. But easier.

 

Now it was different, and they both knew it. Because they weren’t twenty-three anymore, and Agatha wasn’t pretending she didn’t notice things. They’d slept together. They were on a date. The air between them wasn’t suggestive- it was dense. Familiar. Worn-in in a way that made her want to pace herself and speed up at the same time.

 

Which is exactly why Agatha had suggested pool after dinner. Because she needed rules. She needed a space she could bend and twist back into something familiar. She needed something to win at.

 

Because this wasn’t neutral anymore. Rio wasn’t flirting with strangers. Agatha wasn’t pretending not to look. They were here, together, and whatever this was -whatever it was turning into- had already passed the point of denial.

 

Agatha picked up the cue, checked the balance, and chalked it with more force than necessary. She didn’t ask if Rio wanted to break. She never used to, and she wasn’t about to start now.

 

If she could control the game, maybe she wouldn’t have to think about how badly she wanted to lose the rest of it.

 

She broke hard, sent two solids in and pretended she hadn’t lined it up that way on purpose. Rio didn’t comment, just sipped her beer and wandered around the table like she wasn’t watching her every move. That had always been the worst part- Rio never made it obvious when she was paying attention. She just was . Present in a way that made it hard to ignore.

 

Agatha called her next shot with a confidence that she knew would piss Rio off. Corner pocket, seven ball. She sank it clean and kept walking, didn’t give Rio the satisfaction of a look.

 

The truth was, she could feel her. Just to her left. Not close enough to touch, but enough to track. Like heat.

 

And Rio wasn’t saying anything. No joke. No smug comment. Not even a smirk. Just quiet, and the sound of Agatha’s cue cutting the table, and whatever the hell this night was becoming pressing in between shots.

 

 Rio stepped up and took her shot without lining it up properly. The ball clacked off the rail and missed by a mile.

 

Agatha glanced at her, suspicious. Rio just shrugged like she hadn’t just tanked on purpose.

 

“Your turn.”

 

Agatha narrowed her eyes and leaned over the table to line up her next shot. She’d barely settled her stance when Rio, far too casually, spoke from just behind her.

 

“Did you like the nude I sent you earlier?”

 

Her cue slipped. The shot went wide, clumsy and nowhere near what she’d called.

 

Agatha straightened slowly. She didn’t turn around, but she didn’t have to. She could feel Rio grinning behind her.

 

“You’re the worst,” Agatha said.

 

Rio didn’t deny it. She just stepped past her to line up her next shot, mouth twitching with barely contained satisfaction.

 

“You didn’t answer the question.”

 

“I was busy.”

 

Rio sank a shot without looking. “That’s not a no.”

 

Agatha didn’t respond. She stood just beside Rio and leaned back against the pool table. Rio had gone soft around the mouth, the way she always did when she was proud of herself and trying not to show it. It was irritating.

 

And hot.

 

Agatha reached out, sliding her hand across Rio’s chest to the back of her neck. She gave the gentlest tug.

 

Rio moved without question. She let go of the cue, then she turned. Stepped into Agatha like gravity demanded it- hands slipping around her waist, bodies fitting together as if they’d always known how.

 

Her hand slid down from Rio’s neck to rest against her chest, barely pressing, fidgeting with a button on Rio’s shirt.

 

Seventeen years, and she was finally allowed to reach for her.

 

“You remember that Halloween,” Agatha murmured, “when you made me promise to go as Little Shop of Horrors characters?”

 

“You mean the year you said you found the perfect Audrey II costume for me?”

 

Agatha huffed a breath of laughter. “You were so pissed.”

 

“I was pissed! You made me wear a giant foam flower on my head,” Rio said defensively. “Bright pink. And a leaf necklace. I looked like a depressed toddler in a school play.”

 

“You refused to sit down the whole night,” Agatha laughed harder.

 

“Because I had no peripheral vision in that thing! People kept bumping into me. I swear one guy tried to use me as a photo prop.”

 

“You hissed at him.”

 

“He touched my petals!”

 

“You still wore it,” Agatha said, quiet now. Her hand moved again, smoothing over the front of Rio’s shirt without purpose, without thinking.

 

Rio’s grip around her waist tightened slightly.

 

She shrugged. “You asked me to.”

 

Agatha blinked, eyes flicking between Rio’s mouth and the place where their bodies touched. “You’d wear it again, wouldn’t you,” she said softly.

 

Rio didn’t answer right away. She leaned in, slow, pressing her cheek to Agatha’s until her mouth was near Agatha’s ear. Her hands shifted slightly at Agatha’s waist, thumbs brushing once against her sides.

 

Agatha moved without thinking- her arm slipping around Rio’s shoulders, holding her there. 

 

“If you asked me to,” Rio said quietly. Like there was no version of the world where Rio wouldn’t say yes.

 

Agatha breathed out through her nose, barely a sound.

 

She felt Rio smile against her skin.

 

Rio pulled back, just enough to see Agatha.  Their noses nearly brushed. Her hands stayed right where they were, thumbs hooked soft against Agatha’s sides, like stepping away any further wasn’t an option she wanted to consider.

 

Their eyes met.

 

Agatha didn’t look away. She stood still and let herself be seen. Whatever had lived between them all these years, it was no longer hidden behind timing or pride. She held it in place. Let Rio look at it.

 

And Rio moved.

 

There was no lead in, no sharp breath, no shift in posture that warned Agatha. Just the decision, and then the follow through. Her mouth found Agatha’s like it had always known where to go.

 

Agatha felt her eyes close without meaning to. She inhaled through her nose, startled by how much she felt all at once. Her arm tightened slightly around Rio’s shoulders.

 

The kiss was soft. Warm. Her own lips parted beneath Rio’s mouth, breath catching. She kissed her back, gently at first, then with a little more certainty, tilting her head just enough to let it deepen.

 

When Rio pulled back, it was only by an inch. Agatha stayed where she was. Heart unsteady. Mouth tingling. Rio’s forehead brushed Agatha’s, their noses nearly touching, both of them still breathing the same air.

 

Agatha’s voice came quiet, almost fond. “It’s still your turn.”

 

Rio smiled- small, crooked, a little stunned. “Right,” she said, like she’d genuinely forgotten. She lingered for just a moment longer, hands moving once more along Agatha’s side before she stepped back. She picked up her cue again, leaned down to line up her next shot.

 

Agatha didn’t move.

 

She watched her instead- the way Rio’s brow creased slightly in concentration, the subtle tilt of her wrist, the way her back curved just enough to remind her how many times she’d imagined this exact view under different circumstances.

 

Agatha’s voice came quieter than she meant. “You don’t think this is moving too fast?”

 

Rio didn’t look up. “I would’ve married you yesterday if I knew you’d let me,” she said.

 

Then: the soft thud of the cue striking the cue ball, a crisp crack as it hit the others, and the echoing clatter as two balls dropped into pockets.

 

Agatha whipped her head toward Rio, eyes wide.

 

“You can’t just say shit like that,” Agatha snapped, before she could help herself.

 

Rio stood up slowly, turned toward her, and angled her body into Agatha’s space. She shrugged, that same insufferable smirk tugging at her mouth.

 

“Sorry,” Rio offered, clearly not.

 

“You’re not,” Agatha said, sharper. “You’re just fucking with me.”

 

Rio raised her eyebrows. “You want to go to the courthouse and test that theory?”

 

Agatha went completely still. Because the courthouse was obviously closed. Because Rio wasn’t serious.

 

Except maybe she was.

 

And maybe that was the worst part. Not the kiss. Not the smirk. Not even how easily Rio still got under her skin after all this time. It was the way she said it- like she meant it. Like she’d follow through without thinking twice.

 

It was the fact that Agatha almost let her.

 

Just to see what Rio would do. Just to see if she'd really go through with it or if she'd squirm, or laugh, or take it back the second Agatha said yes.

 

Because if Rio didn’t… if she actually meant it…

 

Well. Then Agatha was in much deeper shit than she thought.

Just as Agatha was about to open her mouth, maybe to say something deeply, irrevocably stupid, or maybe nothing at all and just meet Rio’s lips with her own, fully open-



A phone rang.



The sound pulled her back too fast to reality. Agatha’s mouth snapped shut. She turned her head, cleared her throat, and said, “That’s yours.”



A second ago, Rio had been looking at Agatha with a smile forming- barely restrained, wild with hope. Agatha had seen it begin in the corner of her mouth, that shift from playful to something devastatingly real. A smile that would bare teeth, and with it, adoration. Maybe even something Agatha wouldn’t name.



Then the ringtone came, and Rio’s mouth faltered. Annoyance flickered in her features but she didn’t turn away from Agatha. She didn’t even reach for her phone.



“What were you going to say?” Rio asked. She stepped in closer. One hand reached out, resting gently over Agatha’s on the edge of the pool table. The other still loosely held her cue, forgotten at her side.



Agatha didn’t answer. She looked down at their hands instead. Her thumb shifted, resting over the back of Rio’s hand where it covered hers. She brushed against it once.



“Your phone’s ringing, Rio,” Agatha murmured, her voice barely audible.



“I don’t care,” Rio said. “What were you going to say?”



Her brown eyes flicked to Agatha’s mouth -brief, no more than a heartbeat- and then back again. There was no teasing in it. No feigned casualness. Only a certainty that always threatened to take Agatha’s breath away.



And Rio had to stop doing that. Looking at Agatha like that. So directly. So intently. As if nothing in the world mattered more than whatever might fall from Agatha’s lips.



Because if Rio didn’t stop, Agatha might actually speak.

 

And if she spoke, if Agatha gave any part of it a voice, it wouldn’t stop there. Every single secret she’d denied long enough to almost believe was true would spill from her mouth, and fall straight into Rio’s.

 

The phone finally stopped ringing.

 

“Rio,” Agatha said, soft, but with more spine this time.

 

Agatha couldn’t. Not like this. She couldn’t let herself speak something into the open that she hadn’t even admitted in the privacy of her own mind. Even if, in truth, she couldn’t remember a single version of herself that hadn’t, on some fundamental level, already belonged to the woman standing next to her.

 

Rio opened her mouth, maybe to press again, maybe to fill the silence with something gentler-

 

When her phone started ringing again. 

 

And Agatha, to her shame and relief, exhaled.

 

Rio exhaled too, but it wasn’t relief- not like Agatha’s had been. She set her cue gently on the table, then reached into her pocket for her phone. Rather than pulling away, she shifted closer, aligning herself alongside Agatha, leaning in like regret only came when you left too much room for it.

 

And Agatha, who no longer had the stomach to be needlessly cruel, let her.

 

More than that, she moved and let her hand settle at the small of Rio’s back, fingers curling into the waistband of her slacks. A silent reassurance. Agatha didn’t want Rio to think she was running away from her. She wasn’t. She was only trying to outrun her own thoughts. But Rio? She couldn’t leave her behind. Not again.

 

Agatha glanced at the screen of Rio’s phone.

 

It was a FaceTime call from Sage. 

 

Agatha caught the moment Rio’s face softened- barely, but enough to register. And she felt her heart twitch at the sight of it. There was something about seeing Rio worn slightly thin but still soft where it mattered.

 

Rio and Sage hadn’t grown up together. That much Agatha knew. But somewhere along the way, they’d decided it didn’t matter. They’d chosen each other, and the shape of that choice was obvious in ways Rio probably didn’t realize she was giving away.

 

And even with that flicker of fondness, the edge of irritation still lingered on Rio’s face. She obviously hadn’t wanted to be interrupted. 

 

Rio slid her thumb across the screen to answer, and Agatha instinctively tilted her head just out of its frame, even as her eyes stayed on the screen.

 

The first thing that appeared was Sage’s forehead, unbothered and oblivious, until she heard the sound of the call connecting. Then her eyes darted toward the camera. The phone jolted as she yanked it closer, her face suddenly filling the screen.

 

She looked furious.

 

“You dirty little whore,” Sage hissed. “How dare-”

 

“What do you want?” Rio snapped. Then she winced, as if hearing herself in real time. She glanced over at Agatha and flushed, suddenly embarrassed at how fast she’d gone full older sister mode. Rio pulled the phone closer to her face, teeth clenched, and hissed, “I’m busy.” Then glanced at Agatha again and back at the camera.

 

Sage’s jaw dropped. She let out a few breathless, incredulous huffs.“Yeah? Well I’m busy too,” Sage snapped back. “You’re at Bee’s lake house -without me, which is already bullshit- while we’re getting completely fucking slammed! It’s hell. Actual, biblical hell, Rio. It’s past midnight, I haven’t sat down in five hours, and my feet feel like they’ve been fucking steamrolled.”

 

Agatha blinked at the nickname. Bee? She hadn’t heard anyone call Sybil that before. She obviously didn’t comment on it.

 

Rio was trying to stay composed. “Did you call the on-call tech in?”

 

“Yeah, I did,” Sage snapped again. “News. Flash. It’s still not enough. Because three people can’t cover the entire fucking  hospital.” Her voice pitched up, just slightly. “I’m getting fucked in the ass by this shift, Rio. I mean thoroughly. Raw.” 

 

Sage leaned closer to the mic, just slightly off camera now, her voice dropping to a furious whisper. 

 

“Meanwhile,” she hissed, directly into the mic, “you’re off bottoming for Agatha Harkness. Getting fucked in the ass in a very different and probably very literal fucking way.”

 

Agatha bit down on a laugh. Hard. She brought her free hand to her mouth, tried to press it against her lips, but it didn’t help. A loud, choked noise escaped before she could stop it.

 

Rio’s head whipped toward Agatha, scandalized, cheeks already pink. Her mouth opened like she was about to launch into a full defense, but nothing came out. She looked back at the camera.

 

“I… That’s not… watch your mouth! That is so… You can’t just-”

 

Sage cut in immediately. “‘I…That’s…Watch…You can’t just… ” she parroted, mean and delighted.

 

Agatha had to bite the inside of her cheek just to stay quiet. Not because Sage was right, though she was hilarious, but because watching Rio this flustered felt weirdly good.

 

From the moment Rio reappeared in her life, she'd been infuriatingly composed. But this? This was a version of Rio that Agatha remembered. Scrappy. Off balance. Barely keeping up.

 

Then Sage said through gritted teeth, “I need your help, Roo.”

 

Agatha’s hand tensed slightly where it rested at the small of her back. And when Rio glanced at her, Agatha mouthed, “ Roo?”

 

Rio shrugged, soft and almost sheepish. Like she'd forgotten anyone else was listening. She turned back to the screen.

 

Agatha looked away. It filled her chest with something warm and awful. The same feeling she got every time she saw them interact. Every time she caught sight of the photos in Rio’s apartment. A reminder of what she’d missed. Of a life lived without her.

 

And Agatha hated how much it made her miss Lilia. Hated how much she wanted to see them all in a room together. Not for herself, not to be a part of it… just to know what it looked like.

 

Rio cleared her throat. “What do you need help with, Sage?”

 

Sage didn’t answer right away. Instead, she flipped the camera.

 

The screen filled with the hallway outside of the ICU and the portable x-ray machine, parked awkwardly against the wall.

 

Sage started kicking the wheel of the machine. Repeatedly.

 

“This. Stupid. Fucking. Machine. Broke. Down. In. The. Worst. Possible. Place. And I cannot get it to move. Or turn on. Or do fucking anything . ”

 

Rio flinched with every kick. “Hey!” she snapped. “That’s like two hundred grand worth of equipment, what are you- don’t kick it, Jesus.”

 

Sage didn’t stop. “Then come fix it.”

 

Agatha heard the shift in Sage’s voice right away. It wasn’t anger anymore. It sounded tired, like she was about to cry.

 

Rio heard it too. Her tone changed in an instant.

 

“Hey. Okay. Stop. Just… stop for a second.”

 

Sage gave the machine one final, frustrated kick. Then she stilled. The screen angled low, showing nothing but the wheel of the portable and her shoes.

 

“Is it giving you any error codes?” Rio asked, softer now.

 

“No. Screen’s black. I already tried rebooting it. I don’t know what happened.” Sage tilted the camera to show the monitor- blank, flashing black.

 

“Okay,” Rio said. “Alright. It’s fine. We’ll figure it out.”

 

Agatha said nothing. Her hand stayed where it was at the base of Rio’s back, fingers curled loosely at her waistband. She could feel the muscles there, not as tense as before- how quickly Rio had moved from annoyance to care. There was no performance in it. No show for an audience. Just... Rio being Rio, when it counted.

 

She didn’t know what to do with that. Maybe because it was so seamless. Maybe because it reminded her of how often she’d relied on that same instinct and hadn’t realized how much of it had once been offered to her too.

 

She stayed still, eyes on a random wall, not listening to whatever Rio was saying. Her voice had gone clinical, technical, full of words Agatha didn’t understand and didn’t try to. None of it meant anything to her. 

 

But the feeling did. 

 

Agatha realized how much had changed and how much of it she hadn’t been there to witness. Not just tonight. Not just this shift into calm, capable authority. It had been happening for a long time. Rio had grown into someone steadier. More certain. The kind of person people turned to when everything else fell apart.

 

She wasn’t angry. This wasn’t bitterness. She wanted this for Rio. She always had. But it knocked the air out of her every time she got to see it up close and know she hadn’t been part of it. 

 

That the person who used to white knuckle her way through every moment ever had softened without Agatha.

 

Agatha used to tell herself she was done holding out for a version of Rio who never arrived. She had been angry then. Not at Rio for being lost, but for how much of her life was spent resisting- caught in the constant effort of keeping things from breaking instead of letting anything begin. Agatha had made choices without her because she was tired of waiting. Tired of pretending she didn’t already know how it would end. She needed Rio to choose. To move. To do something. Anything. But she never could. 

 

Now here she was, years later, watching Rio be everything she couldn’t be back then. And Agatha hadn’t been there to witness the change. Only arrived in its aftermath.

 

It hurt. Deeply . Because Agatha had no idea if there was still room to be part of the life that had formed in her absence. Or if she’d been gone so long that it had outgrown her. That she had become the one who no longer fit.

 

Agatha would trade anything to go back and make different choices. To stop running. To stop punishing them both for not being ready at the same time. She thought the distance would make it easier. That starting over somewhere else with someone else would protect whatever tenderness she couldn’t name. But all it did was move her to the edge of a life that kept going without her.

 

She wanted to be part of it. Not just the memory. Not just the maybe.

 

Agatha wanted in. Past, present, future.

 

And now, standing at the edge of it, watching it move without her, Agatha didn’t know how to ask if there was still room. If the home she’d walked away from was still there. If anyone inside had remembered to leave the light on. Or if there was even still a chair at the table, waiting for her to come home.

 

Agatha hadn’t answered Rio’s earlier question. She hadn’t let herself think about the answer, even in the privacy of her own mind.

 

But now she did. Silently. Just for herself. Where no else could hear it.

 

‘You want to go to the courthouse and test that theory?’

 

Yes. 

 

-

 

They were back at the house now. It was late, but neither of them felt tired. Neither said as much- they just moved quietly, instinctively, like they both knew they weren’t ready for the night to end. 

 

They had changed when they got in. Agatha pulled on a baby blue tank top and a pair of pinstriped boxers. Rio had reappeared to the living room in white socks, navy and yellow plaid boxers, and Agatha’s old gray Westview U shirt. The same one Agatha had only just realized Rio must’ve stolen from her a few days ago.

 

She didn’t say anything about it. Just looked at Rio for a second too long, then looked away.

 

Agatha sat on the couch and twiddled her fucking thumbs while Rio rifled through Sybil’s vinyl collection, flipping through the sleeves like she knew exactly what she was looking for. Eventually, she landed on Rumors and dropped the needle without even a glance back. 

 

Agatha rolled her eyes at the obviousness of it. But still- classic . She loved that record. She knew Rio knew it. And she chose not to say anything, letting the opening chords of “Second Hand News” fill the room. 

 

Then she watched Rio light a stick of incense- something sharp and smoky that filled the room. It smelled like a Catholic mass on First Fridays, when the priest would swing that metal thing back and forth and the smoke would hang in the air long after the doors opened.

 

Surprisingly, Agatha didn’t hate it.

 

Now the two of them sat across from each other on the floor, the mancala board on the coffee table between them. The marble stones clacked gently against the board. The music spun low in the background. The silence was comfortable, if not a little fragile.

 

Agatha was losing, and for someone who might qualify as the sorest loser in recorded history, she didn’t care. Not with Rio sitting across from her, dropping stones a precision that should’ve been irritating. Her fingernails were still painted black. Her brown eyes stayed focused, head tilted slightly, tongue pressing into her cheek whenever she managed to drop more stones into her store. And every so often, Rio would glance up at her like she was checking to see if Agatha was watching. 

 

Of course Agatha was. She hadn’t stopped. 

 

It was her turn now, but she didn’t move. Her elbow rested on the table, chin tucked into her hand as she studied Rio with quiet focus.

 

“How’d you get that nickname?” she asked, quietly. 

 

Rio looked up. “Roo?”

 

Agatha gave a small nod.

 

Rio shifted, her knee knocking lightly against the leg of the table. One hand drifted toward the corner of the mancala board, thumb brushing over the corner of it.  “Anytime Lilia had to work and Sage was out of school, she’d call and ask if I could come over. Said it was to keep Sage company, but we both knew it was just her way of pushing the whole sibling thing.”

 

“How old was she?” Agatha asked as she shifted her hand forward without thinking, the tips of her fingers brushing lightly against Rio’s on the table.

 

Rio glanced down at the touch, lips twitching. She tapped her pointer finger twice against Agatha’s knuckles, then let it settle there. When she looked up again, her voice was casual. “Twelve.”

 

“Brutal,” she muttered, adjusting so their fingertips tangled together, loose and thoughtless.

 

“You’re telling me. She was weird as hell around me at first. Like, wouldn’t talk, barely looked at me. Just sat there like I was some kind of freak. I think she thought if she ignored me long enough, I’d go away.”

 

Agatha didn’t respond, just raised her eyebrows, she could see that happening.

 

“Then one day, out of nowhere, she looks me dead in the face and says I look like a Disney adult who probably has an unhealthy attachment to Winnie the Pooh.”

 

Agatha pressed her mouth into her hand, trying not to laugh.

 

Rio noticed, of course she did, but didn’t comment on it. She just kept talking, the corner of her mouth quirking up, “A week later she started calling me Roo.” 

 

Agatha dropped her hand from her mouth. “As in the character from Winnie the Pooh?”

 

“Unfortunately,” Rio said, deadpan.

 

Agatha blinked at her, voice caught in disbelief. “And you let it stick?”

 

“It felt like a win at the time. And… I think she meant it kindly.” Rio glanced away, then back at Agatha and gave a shrug. “Eventually.”

 

Agatha huffed a laugh. “Alright. I’ll say it. It’s fucking weird that you have a sister now.”

 

Rio just smiled, lazy and unbothered, her fingers toying with Agatha’s. “You’ll get used to it,” she said softly, like a promise. 

 

Before Agatha could respond, Rio pulled her hand away.

 

The absence was immediate. But before she could linger on it, before she could miss it, Rio was moving. She rose to her feet without ceremony, circled the coffee table, and lowered herself beside Agatha on the floor.



Then Rio was looking at her. Not in a soft, admiring way, but with focus. Like she was checking for something. Like maybe she already knew and was just waiting for Agatha to confirm it. 

 

And maybe Agatha should have been annoyed by the scrutiny, should have deflected or looked away or made a comment that would pull them both back into safer territory- but she didn’t. She let Rio look. Wanted her to. Wanted to be looked at and recognized and known, maybe more than she wanted to keep pretending she didn’t.

 

And then Rio reached up and tucked a piece of hair behind her ear like it was nothing, and Agatha tried not to lean into it, really she did, but her body made the decision for her.

 

Rio smirked, not in the way she used to when she was trying to start something, but smaller, like she was almost proud of herself.

 

“Did you like our date?” Rio asked, barely above a whisper.

 

Agatha exhaled through her nose. “Oh, is that what that was?” she asked, the words light. “I thought it was just two friends hanging out.”

 

Rio’s eyebrows lifted, her mouth parting slightly. “Ohhh, okay,” she said, dragging it out, dry and theatrical. “Just so you know that little crush I had on you?” She jerked her thumb over her shoulder. “Gone. Out the window.”

 

Crush. Right. They both knew it hadn’t been little, and it hadn’t gone anywhere.

 

“Shut up,” Agatha said, smirking now. “You still like me.”

 

“You’re funny,” Rio muttered, not even denying it, voice warm with annoyance that wasn’t really annoyance.

 

“The funniest,” Agatha mumbled back, but she couldn’t commit to the bit. Her eyes were already locked on Rio’s mouth, and her fingers were twitching with the urge to do something- reach, pull, touch, anything.

 

Her heart had already picked a direction, and her body was trying to follow.

 

“Be honest,” Rio said.

 

Agatha bit her lip, still watching her mouth, and gave the smallest nod, not trusting her voice, but managing a quiet, “Mhm.” 

 

Rio’s hand moved again and tilted her chin up until Agatha had no choice but to meet her eyes.

 

“Would you want to go on another one with me?”

 

Yes. 

 

Always yes. 

 

The awful truth.

So the fact that Rio wasn’t turning around?

 

Fucking unacceptable.

 

Agatha cleared her throat- loudly. Aggressively. It was a warning.

 

Rio turned her head, brown eyes soft and stupidly sweet, and offered a casual, “Morning, sweetheart.”

 

Then turned back and started making a second cup.

 

‘Morning, sweetheart’ my ass , Agatha thought.

 

But Agatha didn’t respond because she was too busy picking up her jaw from the fucking floor. Too busy summoning the full force of her adult self not to stomp her foot and scream, ‘Give me my fucking kiss, right now!’ like a brat in a grocery store checkout line.

 

No. Agatha wouldn’t do that. She wouldn’t raise her voice. She wouldn’t throw a fit.

 

She wasn’t a child.

 

Agatha was just going to stand here. Silently vibrating with rage. And wait for Rio to fix it.

 

And if Rio didn’t get her shit together in the next ten seconds?

 

There would be consequences.

 

Real, adult, completely rational consequences.

But Rio still wasn’t paying attention to her.

 

And that thought alone nearly sent Agatha lunging across the kitchen like a wild animal.

 

Instead, she took a single, deep breath. A reasonable breath. A breath full of poise and maturity.  She took one more step into the kitchen. A casual step. A cool, unaffected, not at all very threatening step.

 

Then said -calmly, evenly, like a grown woman very much in control of herself- “So. Just out of curiosity. Are you… not doing that anymore?”

 

“Doing what?” Rio asked, still not turning around.

 

“Doing what?” Agatha mocked theatrically, pitching her voice higher, like Rio was suddenly too stupid to grasp context. “Gee, I don’t know. That thing where you kiss me in the morning like you actually like me?”

 

Rio glanced over her shoulder. “I do like you.”

 

“Oh, well, good,” Agatha snapped. “Then maybe you could let your mouth inform your actions.”

“I’m not mad,” Agatha lied, immediately and poorly. “I just think it’s interesting.”
