“Interesting,” Agatha snapped. “That you woke up, looked me dead in the eye, and then left the room like you forgot how to be a decent fucking human being.”

 

Rio held her gaze, both hands wrapped around her coffee, shoulders stiff in that way Agatha recognized immediately- controlled, thoughtful, trying not to fuck it up further.

 

“I didn’t think you wanted me to,” Rio said, shrugging.

 

Agatha blinked, caught off guard. “Are you joking?”

 

“I don’t know,” Rio said quietly. “You seemed tense.”

 

“I was waiting for you to kiss me, you idiot!”

 

Rio’s whole face instantly softened. She set her coffee on the counter and slowly crossed the kitchen. She stopped in front of Agatha.

 

“Can I kiss you now?” Rio asked quietly.

 

Agatha took a half step back just enough to prove a point. “No. You missed your window.”

 

“Agatha, I’m sorry.” Rio hesitated, then added, softer this time, “I panicked.”

 

That wasn’t supposed to happen.

 

These days, between the two of them, Rio wasn’t the one who panicked. That wasn’t how they worked anymore.

 

It was the last thing Agatha expected. And maybe she shouldn’t have needed Rio to be the one who was always certain. Maybe that wasn’t fair.

 

But she did. So to hear Rio hesitate now -to hear even a flicker of doubt- wasn’t just surprising. It was terrifying.

 

Because if Rio was panicking, then maybe she was thinking twice about them. And Agatha felt her heart drop.

 

Her arms fell to her sides. “What?”

 

Rio stepped forward like she was going to explain, reaching for her hand, but Agatha didn’t let her. She took another step back instead, too stunned to cover it with anything snide.

 

“It’s not you,” Rio said, words tumbling before Agatha could retreat further. “It’s not how I feel about you.”

 

“Then what the fuck is it about?” Agatha snapped, trying not to focus on how her eyes were starting to sting, or how her throat suddenly felt tight and raw, like barbed wire pulling tighter around her neck every time she swallowed.

 

“I didn’t want to scare you,” Rio said, louder, rushed, and breathless. She let out a shaky breath, tried to collect herself, then added, quieter, “After last night…”

 

Dread -full bodied, dramatic, Victorian level dread- washed over Agatha. Dread that belonged to a corseted woman flinging herself across a chaise lounge with one hand pressed to her forehead.

 

She knew what Rio was referring to- the night before, when Agatha had kissed her, and Rio almost said something irreversible. And how Agatha had stopped her with another kiss. 

 

Agatha kept her mouth shut, jaw set, eyes fixed on Rio’s face like she could will her into backing off from the topic. She wasn’t going to ask what Rio was talking about. She wasn’t going to help.

 

Rio picked up on it immediately.

 

“I didn’t want you to pull away,” Rio said, gently now. “I thought if I gave you space, it might make you feel safe. I didn’t mean for you to feel like I didn’t care.”

 

“Well, you did,” was all Agatha said.

 

Just because she couldn’t stomach the words didn’t mean she wanted Rio to pull away. God, no. She’d already been given too much of Rio- too much warmth, too much attention, too much of Rio moving through the world like she was Agatha’s.

 

Anything less now would be unbearable. Cruel, even. A punishment to herself she couldn’t justify, not when she’d already let this much happen.

 

And Agatha knew herself well enough to know she wouldn’t handle anything less with grace.

 

Which was, unfortunately, pretty damning information that she chose not to look too closely at it. 

 

Rio stepped forward and reached out again. This time, Agatha let her.

 

“I was wrong,” Rio said softly, pulling her in with the smallest tug. Her other hand came up to Agatha’s cheek. “Please,” she added, voice thin with urgency. “Let me fix it.”

 

Agatha shrugged, eyes fixed anywhere but Rio’s. She played at indifference, clung to it, pretending she didn’t care- didn’t melt under the way Rio spoke to her, or touched her like this. 

 

A quiet, almost cautious, “Baby.” Then a thumb brushed her cheek, light and careful, pulling blue to brown.

 

Of course that was all it took. Agatha Harkness -world class avoidant, notorious hard-ass- reduced to mush because Rio Vidal had learned how to weaponize a pet name. Disgusting. She should’ve bitten Rio.

 

Agatha looked at her, Rio said, “I want to make it up to you.” Her eyes flicked to Agatha’s mouth, and Agatha’s stomach swooped hard.

 

Agatha gave a tiny nod.

 

Rio nodded back, then leaned in and kissed her- so softly it was insulting. If it had been literally anyone else, Agatha would’ve shoved them off and dry heaved.

 

But Agatha didn’t. She let it happen. 

 

Worse-she leaned into it.

 

Even worser -which wasn’t a word, obviously, but felt correct enough to be insulting- Agatha felt her entire body exhale like she hadn’t once been holding a grudge for seventeen years.

 

She pulled back without a word, brushed past Rio, grabbed both coffees off the counter, then turned around, walked right back, and shoved one into Rio’s hands.

 

“Don’t do it again,” Agatha muttered, already heading outside like that had been her plan all along.

 

No pants. No underwear. Just Rio’s t-shirt and whatever pride she had left stitched into the hem. She didn’t look back.

 

Rio would follow. Obviously. Probably with those stupid cigarettes and Agatha’s old lighter that Rio refused to stop carrying around for reasons Agatha had no interest in unpacking.

 

And if Rio’s idea of apologizing for skipping Agatha’s good morning kiss involved getting on her knees, Agatha’s lower back pressed against the decks railing, a lit cigarette in Agatha’s mouth, one hand fisted in Rio’s hair while she moaned Rio’s name like a prayer- then fine. Sure. That worked.

 

They were in the woods. It was early. No one was around. Probably.

 

And afterwards, once Rio had thoroughly fucked her and Agatha had finally stopped shaking, Agatha briefly considered the possibility of ticks. 

 

She blinked at the treetops, and thought, This is how I get a tick on my asshole and die of Lyme disease.

 

So casually, on the way back inside, Agatha tossed over her shoulder, “You still want that excuse to inspect my asshole, or should I lie down in some grass first?”

 

Rio yelled, “FUCK YES!” loud enough to startle birds out of trees, then sprinted after Agatha like she’d won the lottery.

 

Agatha laughed. Loudly. Couldn’t help it.

 

Unfortunately, Agatha was genuinely concerned about having a tick on her asshole.

 

Thankfully, there wasn’t.

 

No. The real parasite was the woman kneeling on the bathroom tile, whispering, “This is the best day of my life,” while Agatha stood bent over the counter, elbows planted, brushing her teeth and trying very hard not to smile. Mostly because she was too busy questioning every life choice that had led her to accidentally dating her pervert best friend.

The last two days defied explanation. They hadn’t been extraordinary. That was the unsettling part. Time didn’t feel linear. It expanded, doubled back, folded in on itself. Every hour bled into the next, and somehow, none of it felt wasted.

 

They’d moved with a softness Agatha wasn’t prepared for. Slower. Looser. Intimate in the places she used to guard. Long mornings, bottomless coffee, too many cigarettes, and something that felt suspiciously like peace.

 

Rio kissed her good morning every time Agatha blinked awake, and never just once. It was always slow, always drawn out, always a little smug about how easily Agatha gave in. Not that Agatha complained. There wasn’t a single bad thing she had to say about Rio’s mouth… Agatha had checked. Thoroughly.

 

They touched constantly. Hands slipping beneath shirts, along hips, around shoulders. Mouths brushing foreheads, collarbones, the stretch of skin just beneath a jaw. Kisses that didn’t rush. Kisses that asked for nothing but were always answered. They woke up tangled. Slept in. Made coffee. Ate only what was within reach.

 

Agatha kept catching herself watching Rio. The way Rio hummed through toothpaste, tapped her fingers against the counter like she had too much energy and nowhere to put it. The way she sat cross legged on the counter, eating cereal straight from the box, reading the back like it was the newspaper. She was everywhere- quietly, stupidly everywhere. And in the afternoon, sun drunk and entirely too pleased with herself, Rio pressed a cold bottle of beer to the inside of Agatha’s thigh just to hear the way she gasped. Agatha rolled her eyes. And let Rio do it again.

 

They had sex, yes. Several times. Each time different. Sometimes lazy, like it was just a way to pass the time. Sometimes urgent with want, mouths and hands overlapping until it all collapsed in on itself. Sometimes slow, careful, like they were building something from the bones outward.

 

On their final afternoon, Agatha -against every protest- ended up with a fishing pole in her hands. She’d said no. Several times. But Rio had tilted her head and said, “Just once. For me.” So she’d cast the line. Immediately regretted it. Within minutes, something pulled hard enough to nearly yank the rod straight from her grip. She screamed. Rio cackled. Then ran to help her haul in the world’s most pissed off bass.

 

Rio wanted a picture. Agatha told her to fuck off. Rio threatened to pout. Agatha held the fucking fish. It thrashed wildly, and she screamed again, dropped it, watched it flop itself back into the lake. She refused to speak to Rio for twenty minutes. Then Rio kissed her and- well… So much for the silent treatment.

 

Their last morning was quieter. Not sad. Just unmistakably not the same. The light looked different through the windows. The air was too still. The world had started up again somewhere outside the walls of the lake house, and neither of them knew how to rejoin it without shattering whatever they’d built in its absence.

 

Agatha leaned against Rio’s car, smoking a cigarette, while Rio locked up the house- her eyes fixed on the lake. She expected it to look different. But it didn’t. It looked exactly as it had for the last six days, unmoved by the fact that everything else had changed.

 

Agatha didn’t blame it. The lake hadn’t asked to hold their pause, hadn’t agreed to bear witness to what almost felt like a life together. It had just been there- quiet, constant, letting them believe the world outside could wait a little longer. But it hadn’t. And now, standing at the edge of departure, even the water refused to say goodbye.

 

On the drive back, Rio reached for her constantly. Fingers brushing Agatha’s thigh, her wrist, the back of her neck at a red light. She didn’t say a word.

 

And Agatha leaned into every touch.

Agatha pulled into the employee parking lot of St. Rita’s at exactly 6:25 p.m., which left her ten whole minutes to sit in the car and pretend she wasn’t unraveling. Technically, she was early for Huddle- an infuriatingly cheerful name for the pre-shift meeting where the charge nurse handed out assignments and reminded everyone, through teeth gritted politeness, to restock the isolette drawers. Agatha’s only plan was to sit in her car, finish Connections, and summon enough willpower to give a passable impression of someone who gave a shit.

 

She and Rio had said goodbye yesterday afternoon in her foyer, and the memory made her nauseous. 

 

It had been awkward in a way that didn’t make any sense. It felt too casual. Grossly casual… like they hadn’t just spent six uninterrupted days in each other’s skin. They stood a little too far apart, said too little. Rio had gone in for a hug, then stopped halfway through- grimaced at herself like she’d forgotten how to be a person. Agatha might’ve found it endearing if it hadn’t made her want to commit a crime. 

 

It wasn’t that Agatha needed fanfare. She just couldn’t wrap her head around how two people could spend six days sharing a bed- waking up tangled, falling asleep with a face tucked into a neck- and then suddenly forget how to touch each other. 

 

Rio had checked her asshole for ticks, for fucks sake. That wasn’t metaphorical. That actually happened. And now they couldn’t even make eye contact? Please.

 

Agatha pulled Rio in out of spite. Hugged her with more force than necessary. Rio’s arms came around her immediately, and they both went still the second they made contact. They held each other longer than they should have, only breathing, not moving. Then Rio leaned back and let out a shaky breath that brushed against Agatha’s mouth. And then, as if rehearsed, they both let go. 

 

Rio made it to the sidewalk before turning around, walking straight back through the door, and kissing Agatha like she couldn’t help it. Agatha kissed her back, open mouthed and already annoyed at how much she’d missed it.

 

It was messy and ridiculous and briefly obscene before settling into something slower. Softer. Familiar in the worst way. Agatha pulled away first. Rio lingered just long enough to whisper, “See you at work tomorrow,” and pressed one more kiss to the corner of Agatha’s mouth before walking out again.

 

That was the last time they spoke. No texts. No calls. Agatha hadn’t opened their text thread since, and she didn’t plan to. Not because she was heartbroken- she wasn’t. She was just adjusting. A little out of step.

 

Six days of closeness had shifted Agatha’s center of gravity, and now everything was tilted half a degree to the left. She didn’t fall apart. She still liked her space. She still liked her own company. But waking up alone after that many mornings full of Rio’s limbs and Rio’s warmth and Rio’s dumb laugh wasn’t easy. It wasn’t ruinous. Just absolutely fucking irritating. Like the absence of that stupid gap toothed smile had drained the color from her world a little bit. And Agatha had to pretend she hadn’t noticed.

 

Now, Agatha was halfway through grouping four words she was almost positive described patterns when an unexpected knock against her window startled her so violently she let out an undignified yelp, dropped her phone, and screamed “FUCK” loud enough to rattle her own eardrums. Her heart slammed against her ribs as she whipped her head- already halfway into a scowl she assumed would be aimed at Rio, who had a chronic habit of scaring the shit out of her.

 

Except it wasn’t Rio.

 

It was Jen. Which, frankly, was absolutely worse. 

 

Agatha groaned and cracked the window an inch and glared out at her very pissed off best friend. “Jennifer,” she said flatly. “To what do I owe the jump scare?”

 

“Out of the car.”

 

So much for hello.

 

Agatha blinked up at her. “Absolutely not. I have six more minutes to sit here and rot in peace, and I plan to savor every last one. You’re encroaching on sacred time.”

 

Jen didn’t respond. Just stepped back half an inch, clearly waiting, clearly not going anywhere.

“The worst,” Agatha agreed sweetly. The elevator dinged. She stepped out smoothly, tossing over her shoulder, “Feel free to direct all further complaints to literally anyone else.”

She was stashed in one of the postpartum overnight rooms- normally reserved for parents, now repurposed as NICU overflow since the unit had exceeded its capacity.

 

She was starting to think Westview -and every town within a twenty-mile radius- had put a little too much faith in the pull-out method. And judging by the state of the NICU, it wasn’t going well.

No pod chatter, no alarms screeching, no babies trying to flirt with the Woman upstairs. Agatha had just finished her first hands-on time: four scheduled windows in a shift to get everything done: assessments, diapers, feeds, vitals. and all the ritual baby maintenance wrapped in a thirty minute window. 

 

One down, three to go.

“The night before the bowling alley.”

 

Jen leaned in again, practically vibrating with energy. “So let me get this straight-”

 

“You want straight answers, ask a straight lady.”

 

Jen blinked, unimpressed, then continued.

 

“You called out last week so you could spend days uninterrupted being thoroughly, repeatedly, fucked by Rio Vidal? That’s amazing. I’m so proud of you I could cry.”

 

Agatha rolled her eyes and sank deeper into her chair, arms crossed, legs stretched out. She didn’t dignify that with a response- which, unfortunately, only encouraged Jen.

 

“Now- tell me. Is it everything you thought it’d be? Are you actually together now? Because I’ll be honest, I never thought I’d live to see the day you two finally got your shit together.”

 

‘Is it everything you thought it’d be?’

 

What a stupid fucking question. 

 

Because no. Not even close.

 

It felt like Rio Vidal -with her stupid green thumb- had planted something in Agatha’s chest.

 

A garden. Wild and alive and completely outside Agatha’s control.

 

She could feel it constantly, this thing Rio had made in her. Roots coiled around her ribs. Vines threading through her lungs. Flowers blooming behind her teeth every time she tried to speak. She couldn’t open her mouth without fucking petals falling out.

 

It was beautiful. And it belonged to her. Grown for her. She loved it completely.

God. That voice. That tone. The one Jen used when she made it painfully clear she wasn’t the fool Agatha sometimes pretended she was, and they might as well cut the bullshit and get on with it.

 

Jen said nothing else. She didn’t push. Didn’t dig. Just let the silence stretch- long enough for Agatha to get annoyed, which was half the strategy.

 

Begrudgingly, Agatha pressed her lips together and finally looked at her- still silent, but no longer pretending this was a conversation she wasn’t going to have. It was a choice. A reluctant, defensive, unspoken fine, but only because it’s Jen kind of choice.

You and Rio blue balled each other through the most spectacularly doomed friendship in recorded history, and now that you finally did something about it, this is what you’re going with?”

 

And there it was. Jen, dead-on as always. Holding up a mirror and telling Agatha to look. 

 

Agatha resisted the urge to roll her eyes because Jen was infuriatingly right , and she wasn’t even being smug about it. 

 

She could’ve lied. Could’ve thrown another joke at it. But what was the point? Jen had already seen the worst of it.

She’d gotten in her car, heart in her throat, shame like static in her mouth, and driven straight to Jen and Alice’s place. She didn’t knock on the door. She pounded. “I’m hilarious. And you’re in lo-”

“No. Because I’m your voice of reason and gay panic management.”

 

“I’m not doing this with you right now.”

 

“Why not?”

 

“Because it’s mine.” Agatha snapped. “It’s mine ,” she repeated, quieter this time. “And I don’t- It’s too much. I feel like I’m running at capacity and I’m trying not to fuck it up just because I feel everything too hard. Let me deal with it how I need to.”

Arms crossed tight over her chest.

 

“We went on one date,” she muttered. “And played house for a week. After over a decade of- ” she broke off, shaking her head. “Of nothing. It felt real, and it was good, and I wanted it. Jen didn’t respond right away. She just watched her- quiet, steady, hands folded in her lap like she knew better than to move too fast.

 

“You know breaks in the weather still count as weather, right?” Jen said finally. 

 

“Don’t do that.”

 

“Do what?”

 

“Make it poetic and feel safe.”

 

Jen stood, but kept her distance. “I’m not trying to make it safe. I’m telling you that just because it wasn’t in the forecast doesn’t mean it wasn’t real.”

 

Agatha scoffed. “I’ve driven myself up the fucking wall picking all this shit apart. And I’ve decided that it’s not actually that serious. So we don’t have to do all this, okay?”

 

Jen gave her a long, flat and unimpressed look. “You’re so full of shit.”

 

“I know that.” Agatha said, biting it out like it was obvious. “And more importantly? She knows that.” She shifted, jaw tight. “But talking about it like this, it doesn’t help. It makes it worse. So forgive me for wanting to keep her to myself for five fucking minutes without dissecting it like it’s a goddamn case study on emotional repression.”

 

“That’s a hell of a coping strategy.”

 

“It’s better than buying a gun.” 

 

That startled a laugh out of Jen. Lennie stirred.  Both of them fell still, watching as the baby settled.

 

Once the quiet returned, Agatha looked at Jen and said, “I’m not leaving again. If that’s what you’re worried about.”

 

Something in Jen’s shoulders relaxed, the tension easing just slightly. “Good,” she said simply. Then added, “I’m going to hug you now.”

 

“Don’t-”

 

“Too late.”

 

Agatha didn’t resist. She let herself lean into it- let her chin fall to Jen’s shoulder, her arms loose at her sides.

 

After exactly one minute, Agatha sniffed and pulled back with a grimace. “God. That was awful.”

 

“I’m nauseated.”

 

“Don’t make this a thing.”

 

Jen raised both hands. “This? Never happened.”

 

“Perfect.”

 

They stood in silence for a beat too long.

 

“... But if my car is mysteriously keyed again, I promise I will tell everyone in this hospital-”

 

Agatha groaned, “I said I was sorry! And we were twenty-three. Let it go, Jen.”

 

“You keyed the wrong car, Agatha.”

 

“I was drunk and pissed Rio beat me in pool. It could’ve happened to anyone.”

 

Jen scoffed. “It didn’t. And afterward, Rio let you key her car because you were still mad at her for winning.”

 

Agatha rolled her eyes. “She only did that so I wouldn’t feel like an idiot.”

 

“No. She did that because she was more worried about you still being upset with her than watching you key her car.”

 

“Alright. That’s enough. We’re done here.”

 

“Still the most romantic thing anyone’s ever done for you.”

 

“Stop talking, Jen.”

 

-

 

Jen didn’t have an assignment tonight -just tasking- so Agatha asked if she could sit with her babies while she took her lunch. Asked was generous. She told Jen, actually. Told her the exact time, too. Not around 4. Not after a feed. Four o’clock, sharp.

 

There might’ve been a reason for that.

 

Rio, even now, was still a creature of habit. She still counted the seconds brushing each quadrant of her teeth. Still kept her keys in the same front pocket of that same beat up backpack. Still ordered her beers undressed. Still used the back of her knuckles to flip light switches. 

 

And unless the earth had tilted off its axis, Rio was probably still taking her lunch  breaks at 4 a.m. sharp.

 

Jen showed up eleven minutes early. She made a whole performance of telling Agatha not to go over her thirty, but Agatha just smiled, because no one showed up eleven minutes early unless they expected you to run long. Jen knew exactly what this was. She didn’t ask why Agatha was being so precise, didn’t point out the way her eyes kept flicking to the clock.

 

Agatha pressed a kiss to her cheek -loud, obnoxious, sloppy on purpose- and Jen shoved her off with a grimace. “You’re disgusting,” Jen muttered, already settling in.

 

Agatha didn’t look back.

Agatha made her way down to the radiology department on the ground floor, tucked at the furthest end of ER. She took a left into the alcove where five x-ray portable machines were lined up. The space wasn’t labeled, but Agatha knew it was where the portables lived when they weren’t being dragged upstairs or wedged into patients' rooms.

 

She didn’t text Rio. Didn’t wait at her usual smoking spot, or theirs, or whatever it was now. Just showed up. Quietly. Casually. She figured it was a nice thing to do- thoughtful, maybe. Proof she was trying without making it a big deal. She wasn’t going to humiliate herself… not that the bar was especially high.

 

Past the portables and a right turn led into a hallway where the x-ray control booths were. It was the only section of imaging without a proper door, just a wide cutout in the drywall and a scattering of rolling chairs in the hallway outside of it, always in the way. Rio had once called x-ray the ugly redheaded stepchild of the hospital and rattled off a list of reasons so long that Agatha had no choice but to actually listen.

 

She was halfway down the hallway when screaming started- loud, chaotic, and completely unexpected. Then came a voice yelling “SHOT!” and the piercing beep of the x-ray machine firing off an exposure.

 

Agatha slowed.

 

That wasn’t nothing.

 

Agatha paused just before the opening to the control booth, tucked herself to the side where she couldn’t be seen, and listened. Voices drifted from inside- one of them unfamiliar, a woman’s voice, tired and apologetic. “We have to get one more. I’m so-”

 

The woman didn’t finish. A second later, someone -presumably a patient- let out a furious, guttural yell that echoed down the hall. Agatha flinched. It was nearly 4 a.m., and while she was used to infants wailing and monitors shrieking, grown adults screaming in close quarters threw her. The sound didn’t just break the quiet- it tore straight through it.

 

The woman again, less gentle now. “Rio, I need you to hold again.”

 

And then Rio’s voice- steady, almost bored. “Sure.”

 

More conversation followed, low and clinical. Instructions exchanged, a strained explanation offered, the patient clearly irritated that another image needed to be taken.

 

Agatha inched forward and glanced into the booth, just enough to see.

 

To the left, a nurse sat at one of the computers, charting without looking up. On the right, Sage was sat posted at the main console, one hand resting on the exposure switch, the other adjusting the monitor in front of her. The live camera feed showed the patient's pelvis. 

 

From where Agatha stood, she could barely see into the exam room through the control booth’s lead-lined window. She stepped in a little further and reached out, poked the back of Sage’s shoulder. The girl flinched, quick and reactive, twisting in her seat like she was ready to tear into whoever had the nerve- until she saw who it was. Her whole expression changed, irritation dissolving into something entirely far too amused. 

 

“Well,” Sage said, leaning back in her chair, “You’re awfully far from home. Babies are on the fourth floor.”

 

Agatha shrugged. “Was in the neighborhood,” she mumbled, already distracted, trying to peer through the glass for a better view of the exam room.

 

Inside, Rio was geared up in lead, gloves on, standing at the head of the stretcher. There was an orthopedic resident at the foot of the bed- making adjustments, focused, fiddling with something Agatha couldn’t see from this angle.

 

Agatha stepped back slightly out of view, careful not to draw attention. Rio had a habit of always finding her without even trying. But right now, she didn’t want to be found. She just wanted to watch Rio- quiet, selfish, unseen.

 

Sage gave her a once-over, then pressed her lips together and kept watching, like she was deciding how much she felt like starting something.

 

 “Sure.”

 

No questions. No follow-up. Like Agatha showing up down here didn’t need an explanation. Like it wasn’t strange at all.

 

Agatha felt herself exhale.

 

Thank fuck. 

 

“What the hell are they doing in there? Torture?” Agatha muttered, arms crossed as she leaned against the wall, eyes locking on the window- even though she couldn’t see Rio from here. 

 

“Close,” Sage said, tilting her head just enough to be annoying. “Traction.”

 

Agatha glanced down at her. “You gonna explain, or am I just supposed to guess based on the screaming?”

 

“Patient’s got a proximal femur fracture,” Sage said, turning to the monitor and pulling up a previous image. She pointed to the break. “The bone fragments are overlapping, so Ortho applies traction -pulling in line with the leg- to temporarily realign them. It reduces the overlap enough to get a clearer image of the break. Looks awful, sounds worse, but it gives them a better idea of what they’re dealing with before they take the patient into surgery.”

 

Agatha blinked at the screen, then glanced back toward the exam room. “You all just… do that? While the patient is awake?”

 

Sage didn’t answer. She just smirked.

 

“Sage, get ready on the rotor,” Rio called out through the glass.

 

“My time to shine,” Sage whispered, already turning back to the console.

 

Agatha shifted closer to the window, careful to keep herself out of Rio’s eyeline. She leaned over slightly, one hand on the counter, craning for a better look. 

 

The resident leaned in, adjusting her grip on the patient’s ankle, while Rio stepped forward and locked her arms under the patient’s shoulders. Agatha watched the way her feet shifted slightly, grounding her weight, her gloved hands already hooked in place.

 

“One!” The resident called out. “Two!”

 

Sage immediately started rotoring, the mechanical hum of the x-ray machine kicking in as the resident began pulling on the patient’s leg. There was nothing subtle about it. She used her whole body, leaning backward with controlled force, and Agatha watched, equal parts horrified and intrigued, as Rio countered the movement without flinching like she was used to taking the brunt of the resistance.

 

The patient screamed. Loud. Awful. 

 

“Shot!” the resident shouted. The machine beeped. The pulling stopped. Rio let go of the patient and straightened, still calm, already speaking- soft, even, trying to talk the patient down.

 

The patient, for their part, did not give a fuck. They were swearing impressively, hurling every profanity Agatha had ever heard and a few she hadn’t.

 

Agatha didn’t blame them. If someone had pulled on her leg like that while another person held her down like a sandbag, she would’ve kicked, sworn, cried, probably bitten someone- then made it everyone’s problem, loudly enough to get security involved.

 

The resident came around behind the control booth a moment later and began flipping through the images on the monitor, squinting at the alignment. After a beat, she nodded. “We got it!” she called out through the glass.

 

“Thank fuck,” the patient shot back, their voice strained and shaky, still sharp with pain.

 

The resident offered an apology and Agatha felt the nurse beside her rise from her chair, already heading into the exam room to take the patient back to their room.

 

Agatha eased back out of sight, pressing her spine lightly to the wall inside the booth. She told herself it was about being polite. Giving them space. Not hiding. Definitely not hiding.

 

It was inconvenient, how attractive Rio managed to be in the middle of something objectively horrifying. 

 

She was all muscle memory and quiet force, wrapped in lead like it had been custom-fitted, holding her ground while someone screamed directly into her ear. It was ridiculous. Unnecessary. Kind of devastating.

“You held perfectly,” the resident said. “Most techs don’t hold traction like that without complaining.”

 

Sage didn’t look up from the monitor, but her eyebrows rose by at least a centimeter. “Bitch,” she whispered.

 

Rio said nothing.

 

“You must work out,” the resident added, tone just professional enough to stay out of HR’s jurisdiction.

Sage flinched, looked at her, and immediately turned back around like she’d decided surviving the day mattered more than getting involved. She started working faster, dragging labels and slapping Rio’s initials on the screen -standard post-processing, every x-ray needed it- but Sage was acting with an urgency like her life depended on it. Which, to be fair, was a valid read of the room. Agatha knew exactly what she looked like- and maybe Sage wasn’t dumb enough to make eye contact twice.

 

Out in the hallway, Agatha heard the squeak of wheels and the nurse’s voice trailing back through the open door.

 

“Good luck. Seen a lot of folks try to rein the bad boy of x-ray in. Never ends well.”

Her whole body was buzzing, trapped somewhere between walking out and seriously considering the fallout of throwing hands in a hospital. A nurse. An ortho resident. Both. She hadn’t decided yet.

 

She heard the door shut. The patient was gone. The resident, unfortunately, wasn’t. Still inside, still talking- apparently immune to rejection, silence, or common fucking sense.

 

“No pressure or anything,” the resident said, lightly like it was a fucking joke, “but if you have a night you’re free... we should grab dinner.”

Silence followed.

 

Then came a low, guttural sound -half snarl, half bark- and the unmistakable snap of teeth.

She hadn’t even landed on a name yet when Sage twisted around so fast it looked medically inadvisable. Her entire face was lit up- eyes wide, mouth open, jaw twitching like she was about to say something that would absolutely get her slapped. And given who she was related to, it was guaranteed to be bold. Bold and wildly ill-advised.

 

Agatha didn’t give her the chance. She pinched her shoulder, hard, and Sage let out a strangled noise between a gasp and a curse. Then she lunged at Agatha, looking absolutely feral, but Agatha shoved her back into the chair with one hand and zero patience. Sage stayed put, seething, practically vibrating, but wisely didn’t try again.

 

Then the resident’s voice- thin, a little breathless, like she wasn’t sure if she should apologize or run.

 

“Right. I- I didn’t mean- never mind.”

 

The door opened. Agatha couldn’t see her leave, but she heard the rushed footsteps, fast and uneven, like someone trying not to look panicked while absolutely panicking.

 

Agatha didn’t smile. But she was close.

 

Then she heard it- Rio’s footsteps. Getting closer.

 

Agatha turned to leave, fast, trying to get ahead of the moment before it turned into something, but her foot caught one of the rolling chairs scattered around the booth.  She didn’t fall, but it was a mess- one arm shot out for balance, her other shoulder clipped the wall, and her heel caught on the chair causing it to rattle loud enough to announce her presence.

 

“Agatha?”

 

Agatha straightened and pivoted slowly, already composing a lie she wouldn’t believe if the roles were reversed. Something about needing to check on an order. Or tripping on air. Or Sage- yes, blame Sage. That seemed like a solid fallback.

 

But Rio was already there, standing just inside the booth. Her eyes flicked to Agatha’s heel, then the chair, then back to her face- nothing but cool amusement and the faintest twitch of her mouth, like she was trying very hard not to smile.

 

Agatha cleared her throat, nodded once, and said, “Sup.”

 

Sup?

 

SUP?

 

The word landed between them with the elegance of a brick smashing through a window.

 

Agatha felt her ears burn. She kept her face still, but it was a fight. Whatever expression wanted out didn’t belong in public. She didn’t look at Sage. She didn’t have to. That kind of glee didn’t need an audience. It announced itself.

 

“Hey,” Rio said, not smug but maddeningly soft. “What are you doing down here?”

 

Any excuse Agatha might have had evaporated on the spot. She felt her shoulders give slightly, and she felt the corner of her mouth betray her with the start of a smile- but then her eyes landed on Sage, seated directly in front of Rio, teeth sunk into the back of her hand like she was physically holding herself back from saying something stupid. 

 

Agatha looked back at Rio with a small shrug, “It’s four a.m.”

 

Sage immediately dropped her arms and slapped her palms against the desk. “Awww!” she whined, grinning now, turning toward Rio. “She knows what time you take your-”

 

Rio cut her off with a sharp smack to the back of the head.

 

“OW,” Sage barked, rubbing the spot and glaring at her, “I do not get paid enough to be physically assaulted by the both of you!”

 

Rio ignored her completely and stepped past, stopping in front of Agatha.

 

“Let’s go,” Rio said, nodding toward the hallway.

 

Agatha followed Rio out, and from behind them, Sage called out, loud and clearly offended, “Yeah, no, totally fine- I’ll just hold down the entire department alone. Love that for me!”

 

Neither of them looked back.

 

Just outside the department, they passed Teen hauling a portable back toward the bay. Agatha groaned. His eyes lit up.

 

“Agatha! Were you looking for me-”

 

“Not now, Teen,” Agatha snapped, not breaking stride. Neither did Rio.

 

The walk felt longer than usual. Not tense, exactly, but not easy either. Eventually, Rio spoke.

 

“I didn’t see you when I came up to do morning x-rays.”

 

“They’ve got me in a postpartum overnight room,” Agatha said. “We’re running out of space to store the babies.”

 

Rio nodded, and held the door open for her when they reached it.

 

“Bad boy of x-ray, huh?” Agatha said, dry as anything, as they crossed the parking lot.

 

Rio barely turned her head. “Didn’t realize I had an audience.”

 

Agatha hummed, not bothering to hide her lack of enthusiasm. “Didn’t realize you still had a reputation.”

 

That earned Agatha a smile. Predictable. Effortless.

 

“Did you miss the part where I said I’m seeing someone?” Rio asked.

 

No, Agatha definitely didn’t. She heard it. Logged it. Pretended it didn’t make her chest feel stupid.

 

So instead, she said, “You said I bite,” breaking off to lean against the wall of the old administration building. She crossed her arms, waiting.

 

Rio stopped in front of her, the street lamp buzzing faintly around them. “You do,” she said simply, then softer, gaze steady. “Are you upset with me?”

 

Agatha wasn’t upset. She was nowhere near that simple.

 

Because Rio looked hot doing her job. Ridiculously so. She looked hot in those black scrubs she’d chosen to wear tonight. She sounded hot when she snapped her teeth at the resident: unhinged, dismissive, unbothered- as if the idea of anyone else asking her out was beneath consideration. And maybe Agatha should’ve been irritated by the reputation, by the way it still lingered in every room like smoke, even now. Maybe she should’ve rolled her eyes at how easily Rio let the world assume she was reckless, available, untouchable.

 

But she remembered what Rio had told her in confidence. That no one else touched her. That she didn’t let them. That she hadn’t wanted them to. That she only wanted Agatha.

 

And Agatha, for all her pride and reason and pathological need to stay in control, was decidedly not fucking angry. Not even close. She just wanted to kiss Rio- terribly, inconveniently, with an urgency that made her feel foolish for pretending she ever had the upper hand.

 

She pressed her tongue to the inside of her cheek and shook her head, slow and helpless. She couldn’t speak. Not like this. Not with petals threatening to spill out of her mouth, soft and stupid and meant only for Rio.

 

Agatha uncrossed her arms and reached out. Rio took her hand without hesitation, let herself be pulled in like it was the only thing she’d been waiting for all night.

 

Their mouths crashed together. 

 

Rio melted into her, shameless. She whimpered into Agatha’s mouth the second Agatha let go of her hand, brought both up into her hair, nails dragging against her scalp. She opened her mouth like she was begging for Agatha’s tongue. 

 

And Agatha gave it to her. She licked into Rio’s mouth like it belonged to her, dragged her tongue across the roof, the back of her teeth, the soft inside of her cheeks- every part she could reach, just to prove she could. Because Rio had asked for it with everything she had and Agatha wasn’t about to say no to that. 

 

They didn’t stop kissing so much as break it in pieces- barely pulling apart before finding each other again. It was all tongue, all friction, all of Rio’s soft, desperate sounds caught in Agatha’s mouth like confessions she had been all too willing to give. They kissed until they couldn’t. Until breathing became a problem and their mouths were too swollen to ignore it. Even then, Agatha barely pulled back- just enough to catch her breath, just enough to hear Rio laugh, soft and wrecked, head tilted forward against hers.

 

“I missed you,” Rio said, voice shredded, smile twitching at the corners of her mouth.

 

Agatha didn’t flinch. She didn’t soften. She stared at her, panting and flushed, and whispered, “I hate you,” just before dragging her back in.

 

And Rio kissed her again like she knew exactly what Agatha meant. Like she didn’t believe a word of it. It wasn’t gentler the second time. They went right back to it, mouths colliding, hands grabbing, like they hadn’t wasted a second apart.

 

Agatha only hated one thing- that no matter how many times she said it, no part of her had ever, even for a second, been capable of truly hating Rio Vidal.

 

-

 

Agatha had made it through one entire shift without caving. Without inviting Rio over. Without suggesting they crash at the same place, even though they were both working all weekend and could’ve easily justified it as practical. 

 

After their Friday night shift, Rio got pulled into a trauma and texted her sometime around sunrise to say not to wait, that she was going to be stuck there forever. It was short. Casual. Practical. Agatha didn’t respond. She just went home alone and pretended that it didn’t bother her that Rio hadn’t walked her out to her car.

 

She told herself it was fine. Reasonable, even. They were adults. Not everything had to be dramatic. Besides, Agatha figured it was healthy not to spend every second together. 

 

After seventeen years of emotionally compartmentalized bullshit, they hadn’t exactly eased back into each other. One kiss outside a bar and suddenly Agatha was waking up in a lake house, a crash course in domesticity, every moment ripe and blooming and too much. And when they returned to the real world, it showed. Agatha tried to be normal about it, but the silence of her own home after Rio was its own kind of violence.

 

And when Agatha woke up Saturday afternoon, hours before her shift, she was inexplicably, irrationally furious. She dragged herself out of bed angry at the world. Angry at her sheets. Angry at the silence in her house. Angry at how cold her room felt without Rio pressed against her like some living furnace.

 

Agatha told herself it had nothing to do with the fact that Rio hadn’t been there to kiss her awake, the way she had every morning at the lake. Nothing to do with the fact that she had gotten used to it far too quickly.

The rain would speak for them both a little while longer.

 

Tomorrow, maybe, Agatha would try again.

Even after all these years, Agatha still hated seeing Rio cry; it hurt in a place nothing else could touch. And the worst part? Rio still hid it from her, like Agatha hadn’t spent half her life wanting to catch those tears, to keep them safe before they could water the earth.

 

“I hate when you do that,” Agatha said, softer than she meant to.

 

“Do what?” Rio asked, voice muffled under the brim of her cap, the attempt at indifference was brittle and pointless.

 

“Hide from me when you’re hurting.”

 

Rio didn’t move. Her fingers just tightened on her cap like she could pull it farther down, like it offered more protection than it did. Agatha didn’t say anything else. Her hand stayed where it was, resting in Rio’s lap, unmoving.

 

She watched as Rio let out a breath through her nose, quiet and shaky, and slowly pulled the cap from her head.

 

Rio stared at it for a moment before letting it fall slack in her hands. One hand raked through her flattened hair, brushing it back in a motion that might’ve looked careless if it weren’t for the way her fingers trembled.

 

When Rio finally looked up, it was like being let in on something no one else was meant to see. Her lashes were wet and clumped, her cheeks flushed, the skin beneath her eyes raw.

 

It hurt to see and every instinct in Agatha told her to look away, her heart couldn’t bear it, but she didn’t.

 

Agatha swallowed hard and her voice still caught on its way out, “Rio.”

 

“I’m sorry, okay?” Rio said, desperate now. “It was the worst decision of my fucking life, and I’ve lived with it every day since.” She paused, jaw tight, breath catching. When she spoke again, her voice dropped- quieter, but still shaking. “I’m so fucking sorry. I’m sorry I knew exactly what you meant to me- I still let everything happen the way it did.”

 

The pressure in Agatha’s chest built until it was almost unbearable, a hot, tight ache that made it hard to breathe. It wasn’t just anger- it was grief, and years of swallowed words, and the nastiest reminder of everything they’d been before it all went to absolute fucking shit.

 

“I’m still so angry with you,” Agatha whispered through clenched teeth, her eyes burning. “You were my best friend, Rio. You weaseled your way into my fucking life, you brought me into your home and gave me a home, and then you shut me out of it.”



“I never meant to take that from you.” The words rasped out of Rio as if she’d been holding them in her mouth too long, rough-edged from disuse and bitter from being swallowed back too many times. She hesitated, jaw working again, and Agatha saw the shallow rise and fall of her chest before she forced herself to go on. “I just… I couldn’t be around you. Not when you chose someone who hated me as much as she did.”

 

Her gaze dropped to her hands, twisting in her lap, thumbs pressing into each other hard enough to blanch the skin. “It got to my head,” Rio said, softer now, “made everything feel ugly.” She let out a shaky breath that seemed to deflate her. “I kept thinking I’d find a way to be near you without it eating me alive. I thought I had time to figure it out. I never thought you’d leave before I could.”

 

Agatha wanted to scream, to rip something out of herself just to stop the ache. Loving Rio had never been gentle. It grew wild in her, sprawling into every corner until there was no room left for anything else. She could feel it even now-  roots knotted deep, climbing through her ribs, refusing to be cut back no matter how hard she tried.

 

But some things don’t stop growing, not even when you’re gasping for air. The same roots that anchored Agatha had begun to wind tighter, the same vines that had drawn her close were now pulling until she felt stretched thin. And she couldn’t separate the beauty from the hurt. Every petal was edged with a thorn.

 

It shouldn’t have been this hard. Not then. Not now. And yet, they’d both chosen the easier pain: distance, silence, the false mercy of leaving things untouched. Maybe they hadn’t meant to hurt each other. Agatha could almost believe that. But what did intention matter when the damage was already done?

 

She wasn’t innocent in it. She’d hurt Rio, too. She’d stayed with Wanda knowing exactly how she felt about Rio. She’d married someone who made it impossible for Rio to be part of her life, and then acted surprised when she disappeared. She had let the distance settle like dust and pretended she didn’t know how to sweep it away.

 

And now Agatha was tired. Tired of carrying something that refused to get lighter. Tired of tending to a wound that would not heal, of loving something that only grew heavier the longer she held it. The truth she didn’t want to face was that she didn’t want to lose Rio -not at all- but she also couldn’t keep going like this, circling the same pain until it hollowed them both out.

 

Her voice came flat, almost against her own will. “You know what? If it’s going to be like this -if it’s going to keep feeling like this- maybe we should just break up.”

 

“Break up?” Rio repeated, face twisting like the words didn’t belong to either of them. “Wait we’re…” Her gaze dropped, tracing the sweep of the grass under them like she was searching it for proof of something she’d missed, some detail that might make the words make sense. When she looked back at Agatha, her voice was smaller. “We’re dating?”

 

Oh, Jesus fucking Christ. Of course. They hadn’t slapped a label on it, but if it walks like a duck and quacks like a duck, it’s a fucking duck.

 

“What do you think we’ve been doing this whole time?” Agatha’s voice rose, her hand cutting through the air as if she could point to the last four months and make Rio see it.

 

Rio sat back slowly, like she'd just been told something she thought she wasn’t  allowed to want. Her eyes scanned Agatha’s face, searching, stunned. “You’re my girlfriend?” she whispered, almost disbelieving. “And I didn’t know?”

 

Agatha’s stomach turned. Rio was looking at her with those wide, miserable brown eyes, like she couldn’t understand how she’d missed it, didn’t know exactly where it had gone wrong, only that it hurt. Agatha hated how familiar it felt, her own heart in Rio’s hands, still beating, while Rio turned it over like she was trying to figure out when it had gotten there.

 

And okay. Maybe Agatha would take the blame for this one. Rio had been patient, moving at Agatha’s pace, never asking for more than she was ready to give. And now here Agatha was, blurting out words Rio hadn’t even known she’d named, blindsiding her with a definition she’d never been told they were living by.

 

But that was the thing about silence- it could keep the peace for a while, even in good faith, but it always came back to bite them in the ass. It was a habit Agatha hadn’t managed to break, and cowardice had always been her easiest refuge. 

 

So Agatha didn’t explain. She pushed herself off the swing, the chains clattering in protest, and crossed the yard without looking back.

 

“Hey!” Rio’s voice cut through behind her, followed by the sound of footsteps closing in.

 

In seconds, Rio was in front of Agatha, moving into her path, both hands coming up to catch her by the shoulders to stop her. “You don’t get to drop that and not tell me what I did wrong.”

 

Agatha turned her head, refusing to meet her eyes. “Move, Rio.”

 

“I won’t,” Rio said, lifting her hands and placing them gently on either side of Agatha’s face. She tilted Agatha’s head toward her, thumbs brushing just beneath her cheekbones. “Tell me what to fix, and I’ll fix it.”

 

Agatha’s eyes slammed shut. She couldn’t look. Couldn’t let that be what broke her. Her throat locked, everything in her chest felt like it was tightening all at once. Rio’s hands were too familiar, too warm, too easy to lean into- and Agatha could already feel herself losing ground.

 

She shook her head and grabbed Rio’s wrists, pulled her hands away. She tried to step around her, ready to put space between them while she still could. But Rio moved with her, sidestepping easily, her body closing off the path again. 

 

“Tell me,” Rio said, breathless. “What do I need to do? Be softer? Be louder? Pretend it doesn’t matter to me? Just- tell me what version of me you want, and I’ll be her.”

 

The absurdity of it almost made Agatha laugh. It had never been about Rio being too loud or too afraid or too far gone to reach. Agatha had loved her through every version- through fear, through silence, through the years that turned them into strangers. Even now, with Rio standing in front of her, desperate to change something, Agatha still couldn’t find a single part of her that was wrong.

 

And that fucking sucked.

 

Because if there had been something broken- something ugly or evil she could point to and say this, this is why - then maybe she could have let go. Maybe she wouldn’t have carried it for so long, a grief without a cause, growing wild and utterly rooted inside of her.

 

But there had never been anything wrong with Rio. Not then. Not now. Not ever. 

 

Rio took a step closer, her voice shaking but certain. “I’ve kept quiet because that’s what you wanted. And that’s fine. That’s- fine. But I won’t do it anymore, Agatha.”

 

Her voice shook, but Agatha saw it anyway- the shift in her eyes, the weight gathering there like she was about to step somewhere they had never stood before. She knew what was coming. She could feel it as clearly as she did when Rio’s hand pressed against her chest when they kissed.

 

“Don’t,” Agatha snapped, then stopped herself, breath unsteady. “Don’t,” Agatha said again, quieter this time, pleading, because she couldn’t let her say it. Not here. Not now.



Rio’s mouth twitched, holding the words behind her teeth. But then her gaze shifted, like she was choosing a version of the truth Agatha wouldn’t be able to run from.

 

“We’re not breaking up,” Rio said, and it sounded less like a decision and more like a fact carved in bone.

 

Agatha’s head snapped back, her brows drawing in. “Excuse me?”

 

“If you’re going to break up with me, then I’m going to know I was your girlfriend for longer than five fucking minutes.”

 

Agatha blinked, and just like that, Rio was walking away from her.

 

Her chest seized, her breath catching before she could mask it. “Where are you going?” Agatha asked, already moving, her steps quick and uneven behind Rio’s.

 

“My apartment.”

 

The word landed like a door slamming shut, and Agatha stopped cold. She stared at Rio’s back, at the space growing between them, and felt the panic rise so quickly it bordered on instinct. It hit her too fast to make sense of, too sudden to contain. So she did what she always did- reached for the first weapon she could throw- something that might make her stop, even if it was the wrong thing entirely.

 

Rio couldn’t walk away from her again. She wouldn’t survive that twice.

 

The words tore out of her before she could catch them, jagged and unguarded, before she could think better of them. 

 

“If you walk away from me again, I will hate you forever!”

 

Rio stopped like she'd hit a wall. For a breath, she didn’t move, didn’t turn, didn’t speak- just stood there, her back to Agatha, the weight of her stillness louder than anything she could have said.

 

Then she turned, and the distance between them vanished. Her mouth crashed into Agatha’s with a hunger that didn’t build, it detonated. One hand locked around Agatha’s jaw, angling her just right, the other fisting hard in her sweatshirt and dragging her closer.

 

Agatha let her in without hesitation. Tongue, teeth, heat- every kiss a collision, every breath stolen and given back. Her fingers curled into Rio’s hair, pulled, and Rio moaned low into her mouth like it was the only answer she had left.

 

When Rio finally tore away, Agatha chased her mouth, dazed, breathless, desperate to find her again- but Rio held her still, her grip firm, her forehead resting against Agatha’s like she couldn’t quite bear to lose the contact.

 

“Don’t ever fucking say that to me again,” Rio breathed out, the words pressed against Agatha’s mouth like a vow, or a warning, or both.

 

Agatha opened her mouth -ready to throw it back at her, to say then don’t walk away from me again - but Rio had already stepped back, swiping at her face, breath still coming uneven. And Agatha whimpered at the loss before she could stop herself.

 

“I’m going to my apartment,” Rio said, her voice steadier than it had any right to be. “And then I’m coming back. Because that’s what we do now. You can say whatever you want, swear you’ll hate me forever- I’ll still come back. I’ll always come back. And sooner or later, you’re going to believe me when I say I’m not losing you again.” She cleared her throat, wiped at her nose, tried to make it sound casual. “So yeah. I’ll be home later.”

 

And then she was gone.

 

Agatha didn’t move. She just stood there, heart pounding, trying not to fall apart over syllables.

 

I’ll be home later.

 

The smell of Rio’s cigarette still clung to her sweatshirt.

 

Home.

 

Oh.

 

-

 

Agatha didn’t know what she was expecting, only that she couldn’t sit still long enough for Rio to come back.

 

Her knuckles grazed the door once, then again, harder. She stepped back, heart thudding in her throat.

 

The door swung open.

 

“Lilia,” Agatha breathed.
